Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or lead, narrow below with one small opening, and above for distillation. And to press the contents within the distillation, use a well-made instrument of lead for this purpose; and if you see that it is necessary, take a scraper and wrap around the point with cotton; then pour in your oil or juice, and all of the medicines that you see in the reed, and place the reed in the ear. Then insert the scraper into the reed to the full extent of the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled out or almost from the ear; and have the patient feel it within, and the distillations be a small vessel heated over the fire so that it can be distilled in the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	It seems we have reached the end of the text. The title "de l'estoupement des oreilles" can be translated to English as "On Stopping up the Ears". This suggests that the text is discussing a medical procedure for treating ear problems, possibly related to infection or blockage.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to men through blockage of a wound, or a boil inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear, so that it can no longer be seen; and sometimes there is one small hole with pus leaking out of the perforation, and the eye sees this clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, the one that goes deep if it can no longer be seen is of great difficulty in more than one position, and for the one that you see, then place the patient's ear in the sun; and look inside: if you see the opacity apparent, if it has all this thickness then it is its shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cut and scraped in front and behind the entire thickness, if it does not harm the ear; if the opacity is of boil or flesh of the ear, then take with fine tweezers, and scrape lightly, until that flesh is all removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ointment is melted in the ear, take a sharp, subtle razor and heat it up slightly over the fire, then put it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the swelling from the patient's great pain at the ear, pierce lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian balm.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or you take a plug and moisten it in red water, and powder with vitriol broth; and if you see the ear swelling, then it is necessary that you remove the plug and put another damp plug made of rose oil and wax, so that the swelling is removed; then care for it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the pus that has formed comes out, then plunge a sponge and drape it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the purulent discharge, such as treating with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the liquid that comes from papers of themselves when they are moist and dry, so you must stretch them with tweezers and forceps, and cut off the root of a spoonful of its roots; then put on vinegar broth.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if not then peel off, so that he cauterizes with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision is useless; and many times repair, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come on papers of the eyes certain things that seem frost in their form and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture above and below the paper; the works are such: take note if the grandine moves from one part and to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make the width accordingly, then scrape off each part lightly, then grasp it with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a little the paper, then do not harm anything to the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do nothing forcefully, because the ointments will restore it at once and put flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn over the paper, and take the granule with tweezers, and cut it and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is pushed apart by the incision, it does not harm anything; and when the granule is cut, pour salted vinegar into the ear, and cure the area with ointment that brings back flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyelids (possibly a condition known as meibomian gland disease)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that runs in threads on the papers above; it happens more often to children than to grown people, and it hurts them much in their eyes; and they come with catharrs in the mornings, and are unable to look at the light of the sun because the tears rush into their eyes; and therefore they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep on them, and their papers are moist under their eyelids where the inflammation and appearance have covered up the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your eyes and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head in hot water; and then take one linen cloth, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained by the Exirnach of each part, then put it on him; and press at both sides so that the Exirnach be assembled inside the circle; then cut with a sharp instrument in a middle part of the skin a slit of length, and not be more large than the wound which is done to the vein; and make the skin in depth until you come to the Exirnach; and in more arrangements comes out the Exirnach from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then draw it out in one piece of torn cloth between your hands at the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and keep that you do not put anything into the slit, so that you come to all the skin up to the eye, lest you cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the Exirnach does not appear in the beginning of the slit, then stretch a little bit the slit lightly until it appears; then draw it out as we have said, then soak linen cloths in oil and water, and put them on the place, and draw out stitches.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who burn oil on it and put it over to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it until they are healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the warm place, then apply a poultice soothing it until they are healed.
des poilz des papieres	The hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on paper hairs sprout that are not of their nature, and they become inflamed, if they cause harm to the skin, and bring about ways of diseases such as constant tears and softening of the skin and blisters, so much so that it causes destruction of the skin; and the cure is according to four manners: or by cauterizing with fire together, or by a medicine that burns according to what is written in the chapter on cauterization, and is done either by incision and suturing or by stitches, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your lap; then turn the paper with the hairs towards your left hand; if it has changed, well done; if not, take a needle and thread one thread on top of each other; and place this on the margin of the paper where the hairs are sprouting from these hairs, and pull one thread up to the entire length of the paper and turn it under the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the outgrown hairs, a cut all around the spumalike swelling, from the great tear down to the small one; then take one thread and place a small pouch made of cotton and cloth underneath the paper; then sign above the paper a figure like that of a myrtle flower, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see the paper rising with what is divided into two parts.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If the person has need of it, make a great quantity of paper that is softened; then apply the whole saltpeter on the two lines you have signed, and begin with a large wound just up to small; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then insert the wick into one of the two angles of it, then scrape off all of it; then join the two lips together with a stitch of a needle on fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood, and make the superfluity of threads above the two cauldrons on any sticky things, if you wish to do so; and if not, take no care, then leave the stitch and the threads up to three days or four; then cure the wound without a stitch with drying and constricting things, for the paper relives at the sudden of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitch is moist (as said the ancients), and this work is done without fear; and there is another way: and it is that you sign the paper on a figure which is like the leaves of myrtle, as we have told, with three bent wicks according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then treat the swelling with gentle, equal pressures according to its shape which is thus:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with which there is a thread, and stick it in the figure; and stick the other thread near the great lip, and the second thread near the small one, and assemble between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift up all the skin on which you have marked, just as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments that ease; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing in both cases is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the wounds is thus: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two fine ties as long as the paper and the width of the spittle is; and treat the two parts with equal pressure; then assemble one and the other finely on top of what swells up from the oil on the paper, and strain out the two stitches from the two sides properly; and let it be in this way for some days, and the skin that has been strained will die and turn black and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if the wound has some force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper has been lifted, and the hairs can no longer protrude; and this is the form of the two cones that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and put one thread of silk into it softly and finely; then assemble the threads and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be the width of a hand long; then order in the chase another fine thread of silk briefly, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy one; and keep it close to the sun so that the work is highlighted, for it is a subtle and delicate work; then put the needle into all the hairs in the root of each hair, and make them pierce the paper quickly as you pull them out over the natural hair; then extract the hair until it comes out from all the hairs in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is pulled out and the hairs don't come out with it, you will pull out the chase from below all the thread that you have ordered, until the chase comes out through the perforation above and you can see it with the vision of the eye; then you will pull out the chase and the thread, and close the eye and let it rest for two or three days, until the hair has taken its place and the skin has grown back; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and raise it with that one where you leave it, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que vous ayez sauté un passage !
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the soreness comes into the eye, there are two kinds of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.

And the manner of working on it is that you cut through that scab, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linens to sew up so that it heals; and you should not use in its treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease comes back worse than it was at first; but there is a work of things that soften them, such as fenugreek; and the rose of water or else the seed of flax cooked, and an ointment made from verdigris melted in some oil, and I envelop in a cloth, and cure with this.

And the treasure of your cure is that you take care to let it not heal according to its original form; and these works which we have said are nothing but remedies for this disease so that it does not return in its former form.
