puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then press the eye strongly with those threads finely, and suck out the blood an hour after another, until you see those veins outside of the eye being removed; and be careful not to prick the eye at the points of the threadlets, and do this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not miss just those veins; and when you have done this, then distill into the eye greenish-yellow and red liquor to corrupt what is left from the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove all that in one hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains be soothed and you are assured of the absence of heat, then resume according to this manner as is before until it be cured; and this is the form of treatment:
de la fistule de l’oil	It seems that we've reached the end of a medieval medical text. The title "de la fistule de l'oil" can be translated to English as "about an abscess or boil on the eye". This type of text was common in medieval times, where healers and physicians would write down their remedies and treatments for various ailments.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon so call them "arissati" fistules: when you cure it with cautery and hot medicine according to what I said before, and it is not healed, then you make an incision on the abscess there where it should die, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then reshape it with all the instrument that makes this form; and it is called "aspre chief", and it should be made of iron into one sharp point, and pointed like a file as in its present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is pressed; and do this as many times as necessary, then restore the area with drying medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the abscess is congealed, and pus forms, and the body of the boil is congealed, and remains thus for XL days, and it does not renew and is not an abscess, and a bad accident does not occur, you should know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back into its normal position according to this shape: and is that you uncover from bone the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered so take the forceps according to this shape, and be the prongs of iron at III angles, and the handle be thinned all the way up to the end as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the bone near the arm pit, and move your hand away from the eye of blood. Then turn all the way back to the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the vein if they hold their hand over their neck; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened the place, then the material will go into the neck. If this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the end of the stick (or iron instrument)
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the pus finally comes out of the wound completely and there is no further disturbance or decrease in the navel, it is time to bind the patient. Then heal him, then apply leeches or a blister with iron to bleed, then place a compress made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla on the eye. Then strain the eye, and fill the area above with bandages and cloth; and the manner of the cloth is that you take soft cloths, double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount needed by the eye; then bind it tightly above with a strong bandage, and repeat the bleeding with leeches without hurting; then remove the leeches and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the compress becomes wet, you must bind it more tightly. Then remove the compress after the day and night, and if you see the eye healed, it is well; if not, you must repeat the dressing and the cloth and the compress and the leeches until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the rupture or tearing of the conjunctiva (the thin membrane covering the white part of the eye)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the disruption comes in the conjunctiva (conjunctival disruption), and it bursts open, and there are papers coming out like a drop of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you see it covering, the treatment is such that you stick a needle into the root of the affected part down to the surface above, then stick another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the wound; and make it pierce through, and leave the first needle in place; then remove the spot where the double thread was, and tie a part of the conjunctiva around, and bind it well, then pull out the needle and put a moist linen cloth on the eye, and let it stay until the thread adheres to the conjunctiva, then care for the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes when the wound is bound by the conjunctiva from one part of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears large, then pierce it with a fine needle that comes from the center of the eye, and correct the moist albugine (a type of conjunctival membrane) and descend the eye, and go inside immediately; then pull out the needle until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bulb of the eye (likely referring to a specific part of the eyeball or orbit)
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the eye itself being assembled in the eye, resembling water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and upright, then take their head between your hands from two parts, and move them so much as you see the bow coming up to your eyes; then stop and do not let it descend and be disordered by the light, and see the things which are in front of the patient just like they usually are; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descending of the bow is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Make the patient sit between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and place it on the corneal tissue I over the pupil by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the eye liquid issues; and when it is issued, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey or boiled fenugreek and honey, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the waters of the eye (likely referring to a condition where there is excess fluid or discharge from the eye)
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the shapes of the liquids in the division, and what is needed to pierce; do as in work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, far from the light of the sun, and close their good eye very tightly; then put the paper over the eye in your left hand if the eye is to your left, or in your right hand if the eye is to your right; then take with your right hand, if the eye is to your left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or with your left hand, if the eye is to your right; then place the point of the instrument next to the cornea by the thickness of a nail in that blank part of the eye near the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the blank part of the eye, and feel when almagda comes out empty; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the midpoint of the measure of the thickness of the membrane from the pupil to the end of the black part; and that is the cornea of the eye; if you see the bone on that paper because of the clarity of the transparent membrane, then place the instrument just to the spot where the liquid is, then press under a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the eye has descended now, the patient sees it in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the eye has returned to its place the second time, put strength with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not move, pull gently with a gentle hand in turning your hand poco by poco; and then put a small piece of linen thread back into the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put a poultice or wet linen cloth in oil of roses and in vinegar of egg white over the eye, and bind it with a bandage to the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are of our time, place a poultice with abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it happens that it cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some people who have very hard eyes, you should take the instrument which is called "alberit", whose shape is:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in a thread as we have said; and upon completing the work prepare the bed for the patient in a dark place, where he sleeps on his back in the dark; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and keep it tied according to his condition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark place, and examine his sight, and let him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and it is not necessary for you to do this now during the cure or after the incision, but rather wait, because the eye rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the boil comes to a head, instruct the patient to release the eye in front of it on the seventh day, and apply the ointment that soothes boils; and when it is calm, then release the eye and place a poultice on its face for a day or so, and be immediately in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then exit the house cautiously and quietly, and turn back into your own affairs; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the region of Irach (modern-day Iraq), who told us that in his peaceful land, people made almagda (a type of thread or string) pierce their eyes, and it would be followed by the flow of water. However, I have never seen anyone do this in our country, nor have I read about it in ancient books; perhaps it's a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of alum, on account of which one who does not know them sees them; and they are of pure silver:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the head of these is of the same subtlety, and the end in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	de la char sur le nez (expression idiomatique)
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are or are born various types of boils gathered together, some of which resemble scorptions in many feet; and if such boil has a dark colored center, and if it has a soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore, of those boils which are soft and not darkened, it is necessary that you have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, and spit on them, and scrape them off; then take what comes out with a sharp, fine knife from one end, as long as you know that boil is completely opened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that cannot be taken out, you should open it with all one of the sharp, subtle instruments lightly, until nothing remains; and if it swells or becomes an abscess, if the scab is cut off as it should be; and if it are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize it until the scab is extinguished and all the tumors are taken out, then pour vinegar, oil, wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the needle works, and moisture comes just up to the palace, know that it is clean; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new bone in the upper bone, where instruments do not come to cut: then you must put a thread of linen one piece thick, and knotted with many knots, and have between each knot a space at least one finger's breadth; and put the patient's head of the thread into their nose so powerfully, and pull towards something smelling as it comes through the nose into the mouth; and often children do this in school, and it is an easy thing for whoever wants to do it; then take the head that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as long as the thread is.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do what you know that the nout has corrupted that flesh, then take the son, wipe out the blood, and soak the son in Egyptian oil, and put it back in its place just as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all of that which remains of flesh; and then put on the head a bandage of cloth for some days until they are healed, and if they have need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, by which one distills the oils and medicines near-by.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or of lead, resembling an open lamp, like a candle, and it should also conduct; and if you see fit, make a closed candle, and the instrument should be full to purge the head; and have one handle at the head to hold it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	de la char sur le nez (expression idiomatique)
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	A disease called "telul" often occurs on the head of the neck; it grows and becomes large over time, so noticeable to see. And because of this, you must cut it out at the beginning, and scrape away all the scabs; then place on its place the fire cautery or burning medicine. And if one delays cutting it out until it is large, take heed lest it be hard, of foul color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because that is an enchanted abscess, for when one cuts into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is clean in appearance, not of foul color, and you see that one can cut all around it, the patient will empty out and feel fear, and cure the place of scorching and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the swelling is cut and scraped away.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuance comes into one of these working cartilages, it is little profit, as is the case with some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is then necessary to do what occurs with anyone, if you look and see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and at that time join the two lips together with a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from one part and from another, it is necessary for you to scrape away all parts of their skin as long as they heal, then assemble the two lips together with a suture, bind it, and sprinkle above powdered blood of dragon, and incense powder; and put above the powders a piece of plaster of very strong glue or other adhesive plaster, and let it be until it hardens by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the suture is that you assemble the wound with:
des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home some have abscesses in the lips that are hard like grains of wheat, small and large; then you must turn back your lips, and split each one open with a knife, and take out the pus and cut it up into each part; then put vinegar on the place after cutting it, so that the sore is stained; and then let the lip heal by itself, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum flesh.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is a piece of flesh stuck above the gums that the old people call "albulus"; if it needs to be removed, you must hold it with tweezers and cut its root and let it bleed or discharge; then put vinegar on the place to dry out or other drying and desiccative powders; and if that flesh returns after being cut, and many times happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come back after cauterization; and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the sores.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the gums, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and ugly scabs; and sometimes the teeth turn black and yellow and green, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth stink; you should make the patient sit in your hands, and his breath be on your holy person, and pull out the teeth or scabs that appear, until there is nothing left; and do the same with the blackness and yellowness and greenish discoloration and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if you take out the first reason, it's good; if not, repeat the second day and the third, until you have everything extracted; and know that teeth need different forms of instruments to extract them, according to what the job shows, because the extractors who remove teeth from between the gums have different shapes than those who remove them from the head of the gum; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you cure the tooth of its pain, it's good to delay drawing it out as long as possible, because that should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance so that there is no excuse for pulling it out. (Note: This text seems to be recommending against performing an extraction too quickly or without proper preparation, possibly indicating a warning about the risks of tooth extraction in medieval dentistry.)
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When then the patient is constrained to urinate, you must be certain of the urine's quality.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the patient departs and he believes it is the good water, and has him urinate the good water; and nevertheless the pain does not depart by this, until the bad water exits, for we have already seen to do to these sinners; and when you are well certain of the urine's quality, you must scrape around the tooth with a sharp instrument on all sides, then move it back and forth with your fingers or fine tweezers at the first point and point, until they are well separated, then secure the tweezers well; and the jaw of the patient should be in your hand between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not go out easily, then take one of these instruments and insert it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you should fill it with cloth, at the place of the hole; and if it is strained slightly with pincers, that it does not break when being strained; and you must work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and report to the patient by the wickedness of the root more great pains than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act in the same way as ignorant surgeons do, who by their haste and boldness break the jaw sometimes, and do not bring about what we have described; but often they bring about great illness through the roots that remain or because they break the jaw, as we have seen many times. And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the place with wine or with aloe and gall; and if there comes bleeding from the wound, which often happens, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	Il semble que la conversation soit interrompue. La partie qui commence avec "Les formes des estrumens..." n'est pas clairement liée au contexte de l'extraction d'un dent, mais plutôt décrit des instruments chirurgicaux en général.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may they have large limbs that do not bend at all when walked; and may they be of iron well made, and may they have teeth so that they can hold fast.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains on the outside, you should put moist cotton or butter on the place three days or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the place is soft, put in forceps called "algefri", by which the bone seems to be like a sucking animal's mouth; and inside they should be made like a file and it is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you expose the flesh completely around the root, and then put in the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a plane, by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And may it be strong and thick so that it does not break; and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, by which these forms come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need to use this instrument that has two blades, by which it is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fasteners that are in front of the root of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large forceps, by which it is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And may this instrument be strong so that it cannot break; and know that there are many instruments for teeth, and also other instruments, not counted among them. And the wise master craftsmen find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach a tool due to the diversity of them, and do not break the bone or the other bones, or if they do, then he seeks the instruments that it is necessary for him, as I have told you, and helps from gestures, by which this is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	It seems that the text is describing a surgical procedure for removing teeth. Here's my attempt to summarize it:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and its form is ugly, and likewise in virgins, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot polish or file it: then cut it. And if it is close with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape I have drawn, and it is similar to a small beak, and made of iron pointed at its end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the chisel is short and short in hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, take a file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth short and short in hand lightly, so that it does not move until it breaks; then smooth out at the end with a very sharp razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is knocked out by percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press on them what they chew without them falling, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and it does not work; then you should restrain them with a thread of gold, for the threads of silver become green and rotten, but the golds never change; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width of the space between the teeth; and if you want to join the teeth, take the thread and insert it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the tooth in question between the other teeth, as many as there are one or more, until you see it firmly enough up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start again with the covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and skillfully, as long as it does not move; and let your thumb be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Cope the hairs of the thread with a pair of pincers, and assemble them, and insert between the healthy tooth, and put so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then let him be thus tight as long as he can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, if strained by another thread; if it stays and serves in this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the binding of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one should replace it fresh and fresh, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and patient meddle with it; and at times one makes the shape of a cow's rib tooth and places it in the place where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and it will remain and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut off the string from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At times this thing comes under the tongue or natively, which one knows to do thus; or by accident of a sewn wound; and the operations are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your healthy eye, and lift up the tongue; then seize the nervous string from the wide part, as long as the tongue is disengaged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, it is a sign of a sewn wound, so insert a splint and cut from the wide that bond; and take care that the fissure is not too deep, for the artery which is under it; and when you have done this, then lift up the hot iron or gentle, or cold water, and put under the tongue a linen tent; and soak the patient every night, so that the sore does not join.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if hemorrhage comes from the wound, then place verdigris on the place of the wound; and if blood flows, then cauterize with the slow cautery lentiginous, which is good for that; then cure him with another treatment until he be healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the sore is of a foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it declines into a suppurating wound, and there is moisture, let it drain out and make a fine paste from a gentle salve, and deliver it on one part and the other; and if the discharge comes to your work, put vitriol powder on top until it is effaced, then return to your work until you extract all the pus; then lift the joint with thread and silk, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there comes within the throat swellings called "godath", and they are properly called the almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hardened abscess of small sense and pus-colored, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the hemorrhage; but leave it until it be dead, and then you will cut it out, or else it would break on its own; and if it is of white-colored rent, and the root is fine, get ready the instrument to cut, but first examine if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then cause the patient to sit in front of the sun, and his hands should be clean, and tie him gently with the servants between his mouth and his head, and press the tongue onto the instrument that is this form; and it should be of subtle silver or fine tin like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with this instrument and see the swelling? Then take a small needle and insert it into the almond, and draw out the pus above as much as you can. And remove any thread or filament that comes with it, then cut off the top with the instrument, which is its shape, resembling a scissor-like forceps. Although the chief part is curved, one end to the other, and very sharp, it is made of iron or lead.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have that instrument available, cut off the swelling with a pair of forceps, which are shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And the forceps should be sharp on one side and dull on the other. When you have cut out one of the almonds, then cut out the other in the same way, and after making an incision, gargle the patient with hot water and vinegar, and if there is bleeding, gargle the patient with water or cooked apple peelings or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops. Then cure the area until it is healed. And if other swellings arise in the throat besides the two almonds, then cut them out in the same way as the first two, without hesitation.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I healed a woman from an abscess that was new inside her throat, that is to say the small-sense abscess; and I had well closed all the throat so that the woman could not exhale because the canal was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so large that I had to make two drains through the two openings of the new flesh.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then hastened at once, and inserted an onycha in one of the openings, then the pus flowed out, and a great quantity of blood came out; then I refilled another part through the other opening of the new flesh, and made her open her mouth and press her tongue; after that I inserted the onycha into the abscess, and it drew out some part, and only a little bit of blood came out; and thus was the canal of the woman's throat unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease from cutting off parts of this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again at once, and filled the place that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I bound it up and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those areas, and only knew what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	from the urine
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the membrane descends to the eye and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under the fat and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the swollen abscess has been relieved, and she is subtle, then you must cut into her; and that one which is round assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of dusky color or black, then you must avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres. Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And say to the chief one of the sick person that he put a cloth over his head or on the place where the medicine is placed, as with a ladle's spatula, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye; and have the sick person lie on their side so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat or the wound. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press on the eye with the quantity of half an hour, until you see it become darkened and the irritation of the medicine is calmed; and if you see this, take cotton and wrap around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into all the cotton above, so that the cotton becomes hard on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wait after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, then restart it, and afterwards cleanse around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean up what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargling until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	It seems that the text is describing a medical treatment for an eye condition. de la sansue de la gorge	of the swelling of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.
