li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what remembrance comes after this in the book from both sides, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways in which one is its own kind, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses on the fat part are different from those which come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is soft according to its completion; and of those kinds which it is necessary to pierce when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and they are left until they become soft all around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint have rotted, whereby it is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is near the main member and you delay perforation until it is soft, then it will harm the main member; or if it is near the fundament, so that when you pierce it while it is soft, then it will spread inside and become fistulated and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time for piercing an abscess that is dead according to its completion, and that is when the pain has subsided, and the fever has broken, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the decrease in swelling and hardness of the head of the abscess, and other signs. And you should make the perforation sit in a position more dependent on the location of the abscess, and where it most protrudes; and the perforation should be as long as possible, and if the abscess is located near the hands or feet, or in joints, nerves, or arteries, or in any other places where there is no bleeding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who suffer from, by displacement of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the fatty part of the skin, it is advisable that you leave the opening until it has been confirmed to be fully digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before they have come out, the body of the venom will be hardened inside and will be full of thick pus; and possibly the lips and the deep parts of it will become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that has been pierced according to the width of the body, as necessary for the member in which it lies.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should make small openings in small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover them; when it has become as dry as a piece of cloth, and is softened, then you should do similarly to what one does with infants: and if they are cut into three angles, and if they have been cut like the leaves of myrtle, such as abscesses from gangrene; and if there are such where you make a circular incision, and other shapes and kinds of incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as a soft and superficial abscess, it is necessary that you make a thorough puncture; and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has accumulated great pus, and you puncture it, so do not pull out all the pus at once, but pull out some of it; then stop the abscess just until the next day, then pull out something else again from it; do this in increments, many times a day, until all the pus is gone; likewise if the patient has weak virtue, or women bearing children, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus is boiling up at times with the exit of the pus, lest by chance the patient dies, and you do not take heed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then beware this chapter with great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, if the wound overflows, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a plain incision, then stitch up with linen or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many pustules, it is necessary that you put a poultice in each one so they come together against each other; and if you have cut out part of the skin from the abscess, and you have covered it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or a strip of linen cloth damp, and tie it just until the next day; then remove it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, then administer cold water and vinegar easily, and moisten the cloth, and apply it to the place of bleeding repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding does not cease, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said to be used on clean wounds in this book, and if it is summer time, and the place or the abscess is very moist and nervous, then you must put on wet and hot tents and cloths with wine and oil; and if it is winter, and the place is fleshy, then you must put on wet and hot cloths with water and oil, or with cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then release the abscess and drain and cure it, as needed, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have told you how to proceed before starting the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Ulcers
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When a boil comes on the head, small abscesses appear, and they are mannered like spider webs, just as the nest of a hen, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and of the same kind as which have moisture like pus; and if there are such that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt that the abscess will not change its course.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of cutting are such that you must try with all sorts of instruments which are called "entromissoires", from which their shape comes after, what thing they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make it by placing on top of the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape it with nothing left of the skin which contains that moisture, for it comes back again if you leave anything there; then dip cloth in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and vinegar, and pour the salve into the wound, and let it be until the next day; and those will run out who remain of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then you must start again with the lint, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain at night; then treat the wound with ointment as necessary, until they are healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess keeps growing in size, then cut into it according to this shape, longwise; and you throw in needles, and scrape off from all sides, and put all your treatment of drawing out pus from within the shirt where it is located; and if the vein makes resistance, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this with an abscess that is purulent, and to cut into it and to treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the scab on the purulent abscess and the moist one is lighter, for it contains some blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses or head which do not have any moisture, and one of the abscesses that I saw on a woman's head; and I found the abscess just like a hardened stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if they had made incision into it, they would have done just as much damage as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or on the head, which are those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent place, so that the pus may issue forth; and they are cured as it is necessary.
des scrophules	Il semblerait que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and below the shoulders, and in the groins, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are much swollen, and are joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each swelling is properly inside its coat, just as the boil and the abscess of the head, which we have said; and the likenesses of these swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are boils that contain moisture, and some malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one then that you see of good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and is motionless from all sides and is not swollen towards the neck or artery or conduit, and is not deep; it is necessary that you cover it over, and scrape off each part, and apply the two lips of the caustic to the edges, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and take hold carefully, and make sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and be careful not to burn the flesh too much, nor see too far ahead so that you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it will not let you work, then put vitriol paste, or some powders that prevent bleeding, into the wound; and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you have completed it; and then inquire as to whether any small scrofulas remain, if so, cut them and clean.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, it is not necessary for you to cut this scrofula at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall down without doing harm; then fill the wound with old linen dipped in Egyptian oil, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, then it is necessary that you sew together the two lips of the wound, and tie them now, since there is no surplus to remain because of the great size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand how to cut off the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have superfluity, perforate them where they most bleed; and the perforation similarly to that one mentioned before, hanging down, then attach tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply a salve made from fat, until it is healed.
de squinance	of a swelling
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old people talked and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have dislocated, the cut of the throat that is called "epiglottis" must be removed; and they do not help with this, because all the voices and the voice box of the patient are attached to those who have a boil hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two ears.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the voice box, it must be closed to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four small incisions across, between the two circles or in proportion to the size of the incision through the sinew, not in the cartilage; and those points are then suitable for cutting the epiglottis because there is no fat, and the vessels are long and deep.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the joints, then cuts the skin as far as it comes to the chin; and escapes the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then closes the syphilis, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein at the chin which bursts forth through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice; and leaves the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound on the cut skin, and sew it all together except for the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I think you meant to say "Albuchasme dit" (Albucacius says) rather than "Albucasim dist". And here's the corrected sentence:
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglote because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the dagger, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the womb; and I was called to cure her, and found her thus as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that she had not cut too narrowly nor carelessly the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and sewed the wound, and cured her so that she was whole again; and it did not harm the young woman except that her voice turned red, and after a while she returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglote there is no cause for fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat (i.e., the throat being cut too deeply)
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of jasper, and it occurs very much in women; and it occurs according to two manners: natural, and accidental; or if natural has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fatty tumours, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from a vein; and there is fear, and it should not be operated on with fire except in that which is small, and you prove and search all the surroundings: if you find it just like I said is fat, and cannot be drawn out by any means, then cut it, as one cuts fatty tumours, and treat it all its head; if there is no abscess, then search well entirely, and cure it as it should be, until it is completely whole.
des nous	of the navel (i.e., the umbilicus)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are ours, through which I will say all similarities; and now it behooves me to tell the entire difference that is between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an umbilicus (issue) is hot and feverish, as long as the bubbling is not passed, and the corruption is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the abscess there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it has pus, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins as well as a blister, and becomes large; and they are in two appearances, either thick or moist, and much of color are so as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is fitting, when you come to treat the navel, that you first investigate and examine it thoroughly with all the instruments which are called "entrails", according to its shape, whether it comes out as a cord or a scroll, which comes afterwards.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses of us is that you take or the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two needles back and forth, as long as you know that the instruments have pierced to the core, then when it be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the instrument, and beware lest something bursts.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes out of the ulcer, whatever its color may be, do it as I said for other abscesses; and if after the poultice no moisture comes, know that it is greasy, so do it then in a cross shape, take hold of it with pincers, and scrape off lightly from each part and towards the armpit where it lies, and you will lead it out safe with the new [bandage]; and if you cannot lead it out safe, then lead it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there remains nothing, it will come back many times; and if one small piece remains and causes pain, you should dress the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, hold the wound in place, put on soothing things for the abscess to heat up, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the pustule is large, cut off both lips of the wound, and cure what remains of the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is against you or some other contraindication that makes you rush and apply the place with vinegar broth, let it sit for two or three days, until the wound festers, and the bubbling of the blood subsides; then come back to close what remains from the navel.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the translations:
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the tumors are of many likenesses, such as you see here: great, medium, and small; and there are tumors that have two shapes in three ways also; and there are tumors that have three shapes, and they are in the same three ways; and there are tumors that have two shapes, and single tumors with a single shape, and they are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharp-edged, and there are such that do not cut more than from one side, so we scrape the nerves, for this reason we cannot cut the vein or nerve; and among these introducers are the awls rebounding in cloths, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of the abscesses; and they come in three ways: great, small, and medium, as you see; and one should not use more than in a fleshy place, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes we make another instrument small, resembling scrapers of splinters, according to this shape, with which we staunch blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is put in places where the skin heals after being cut around veins and arteries, and they are shaped according to this large form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Some women's breasts become inflamed in certain men when they start to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wants to cure them should do so according to this shape from line .b. up to line .g..
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine made from boiled meat, then bring together the two lips of the wound at a suture, and heal it until it is sound; and if the breast inclines downward, and is swollen because of its size as happens in women, so you make it into two compartments above, by two similar cuts; where one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then scrape off the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suture and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is sound; and if it is not sound, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the clotting of blood, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it suppurates the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is sound.
des apostemes des asselles	The swelling of the armpits.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These swellings that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula or abscesses with sinuses, and there are some that contain moist fluid.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be bandaged according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g..
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole cavity within the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and let it be until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with suitable ointment as needed until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar nature to scrofula, then cut it as we said in incisions for scrofula, and if the wound forms a cavity, then apply cautery as we said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The rupture or bursting of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin that is over it is sewn together, so many times abscesses occur, and also it happens that the vein is filled and an abscess forms; and if one knows thus when it is because of the artery, then the abscess is long in depth; and when you feel it with your elbows, you will feel it somewhat; and when it is because of the vein, it is reasonable to appear far outside; and it is folly to cover this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and angles and neck and in many other places, and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must apply the fire cautery, and also one who is on the head must do the same, and in that who is filled with artery make by above the skin very long; then open the wound up to the incision, and part the artery from the veins, so that it be discovered; then insert under it a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have instructed you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in temples; then tie the place between the two strings with an instrument so that the blood flow out, and be released the abscess; then apply the dressing when it is all worn out, so that the string falls off; then treat those with ointment suitable to them, until they are healed; and if the abscess is due to the cut of the vein, you must dye your hand with what comes from the abscess on all the skin, then insert a needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and have one double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I said to you, or string of one of two parts up to both shoulders of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread does not come out easy, then insert another needle into all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and bind the threads in four places; then cover the abscess so that the superfluities come out, then cover the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied; then put on the damp cloth with vinegar and oil, then apply dressings and ointments until it be healed.
des apostemes des ners	The swellings or abscesses of the nerves.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses come in arteries and veins when they are inflamed or damaged from overwork or similar causes, so too do abscesses come on the nerves.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	It happens most often in the joints and limbs of those who lift heavy loads, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of the flesh; and it has many dispositions without pain; and when one presses on it firmly, the patient feels pain, but not in the deepest part of the body, but beneath the skin; and it can be seen well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward; and that which is in a joint should not be opened with iron: perhaps there would be contraction; and he who has it on the head or on the forehead, makes a patch on the shoulder blade.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, take it with pincers and cut off its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a string, and scrape it, then extract it and sew up the wound to the suture, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	The large hanging boils or abscesses.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At some times it happens in the belly and not elsewhere on earth; and it is an illness that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to them; and it is the subtle roots and the large heads; and there are small ones and very great ones; and I have seen a man who had two in his belly which were more similar to fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were open so they ran with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them off and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six pounds, and the operations in incising them are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and has thin roots; if it cuts with a sharp blade, and they should be present before you with a cautery at fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For the surgeon comes often very great outflowing of blood, and if the blood vessel bursts, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient trembling and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made piece of cloth, and bind it to the vein as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not stop restraining the cloth until it touches the vein, and choose by him sensible work; and if the roots are large, then be afraid to cut them straight away for the belly, but you can well cut half of them, then cauterize so that they will not return; then cure the wound, and beware that you do not cut the thread which is of bad color and poor sense and white regurgitation.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an infected abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the swelling subsides.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling of the belly comes from cauterization of a wound or a rupture of an abscess, and is above the belly and in some of the intestines, as it happens in other openings, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from windiness; and if this is by the rupture of the abscess and by the issue of the bile, then the color of the swelling is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and apparent through diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it becomes more complex. And when one presses it with their hands, it comes back and returns, and perhaps it is hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bowel and for intense labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and appears well when you press it with your hand, not constraining; and if it is due to blood, then it shows by these signs the swelling being thick and hard, and it is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to touch, and the treatment is that you should see whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It seems advisable that you leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowel, then it seems advisable that you command the patient to strain his urine and have it be straight, then sign a circle around the belly; then command him to lie on his back for a long time between your hands, then go around the place that you have signed with everything in its surroundings; then lift half of the swelling up to the highest point of the incision; then tie it tightly around with a strong thread or a cord made from strong silk, and have the ends of the stitches secure; then work on the part of the swelling that is stretched out over the stitches, and put your index finger in and search for the intestine; if you find it caught up by the stitches, then release it, and push the intestine back into the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take hold of it with the needle, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or vein gives you trouble, then go around them carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads on them, and put the needles through what you have done in a cross shape so that you make a hole; then strain the swelling in four places over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it falls apart, and let the dead flesh come out by itself; or you cut it when it becomes subtle and has fallen apart, then cure what needs to be cured, and remove the swelling as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is needed, and close the wound.
dou chancre	A boil (or a tumor)
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of boils, and how one should treat them with medicine, and how to avoid using iron as a cure; and we say that boils begin in the groin, and there is great caution in their treatment, and the ancients said that when boils are in place where they can be cut out, such as those in the armpits, and on the thighs, and in similar places, one should remove them all when they first appear; and when they are large and old, it is not necessary to approach them, for I have never seen any heal; nor has anyone ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in place where one can remove it, such as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black coals once; then make them drink something to clear their repletion, then prepare the patient for the operation; then take your hot iron or boil, and cast it onto the boil, and draw out all the pus from every part, and remove all the bad flesh without leaving anything behind; and leave the wound open completely, and press well on the place with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the bleeding stops; then cure it with some other cure until they are fully healed.
de ydropisie	It seems like you've written a single word: "ydropisie".
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is but one; and one must not touch with iron to these two likenses: that is to say, tympanites and hydropsy, for they are mortal things; then when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as dyspepsia and flatulence and likenses: if one must not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should so work: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the ministers press the belly out thrusting water to the lowest part of the navel, then take the spatula with the spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And there are two parts to incise.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and all the while it is not so deep that it can come up to the intestines when you stick it in, and cannot wound it; then see if the dropsy is drained towards the intestines: if it needs be, you split open on top of the abdomen three finger-breadths from above the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then your incision should be on the left side of the abdomen three finger-breadths; and if it's due to spleen, then on the right, and it's not necessary that the patient lies on the incision so that the superfluities do not run towards that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and fill it, and lift your hand to all the space between the skin and the belly in as much quantity as an eye nail or a little around; then pierce the belly until the space comes up to the eighth part, and that is the place of the water, then scrape it clean, and I put this instrument which is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is like a silver chain and is of lead or light iron, and in the lower part has a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the shoulder blade is shaped like a feather, and this is the form of the incision from which the writer cuts the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is a handle, so that when the instrument comes to the water, you now lift it up over the instrument; then empty half or one-third of it, because if you empty more than what is necessary at this time, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of their spirit from the arrow, or they faint, or approach death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the disposition of the virtue of the patient signifies, and his pulse; then pull out the instrument and hold the water, and it is now held by the cure that stops the hole which is on the side, for which I have spoken, so that you pierce in this manner; then start the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and pull out a small quantity of water; do this each day, and be careful not to exhaust it until there remains only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt about the patient, and you leave them for a long time in water, then treat them with scalding sand or hot sand, and by pouring out sweat or bathing and being in the sun, and if it turns to drink; and treat them with desiccative medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the strangulation of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary that he immediately have an incision to all the thickness of the foreskin very subtle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put the subtle plug of cloth into the opening and tie it and hold thus for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, then remove the plug and let him urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps there will be no need, because the urine that comes out does not leave the opening closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose hernia is small, must take medicine of poppy seed, as we have said, so that it will spread.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hernia in its place are blistered, for none are born with a hernia at the head of the penis, so that they cannot urinate until they lift their penis high; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come down to the scrotum, and this is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of this treatment is that the sick person lies on their back often, with the top of the penis and the glans (or head) as small as a pen's nib, so that the opening points downwards, as it should; and they guard against discharging blood which comes out many times; and if there is bleeding, they apply what stops bleeding to the wound, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Cil qui a pustules sus sa verge doivent prendre des huiles douces et de selz pour le guardeir, car il li convient que la matiere ne se coille en lui; et si il veut faire uriner son urine, il doit estre ostez li clos, et puis remet, selonc la maniere de qui nous avons dit avant.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this condition comes in the scrotum, and it is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant ones and non-malignant ones; so you should take them out with a sharp instrument and clean them all, then put on moistened cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then cure them with refined oil until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of foul colour and before time, it is necessary to bring a cauterising tool there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have opened it, and the boil is on the penis and has part inside the skin and part outside, it is necessary that you remove the boil which is inside first; and when it is closed up, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you treat it together, you are not assured that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and a blackening and corruption comes in its root and into the scrotum; so you must get rid of all that is black and corrupted. Then apply on the plaster made of ground hazelnuts and dates, then cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there comes a discolouring of blood, so make the lunar cauterization in this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization helps in two dispositions together: that is to say, at the discoloring of blood, and at the corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must then make a little pipe from the tube of the penis, and have the patient urinate through it; and when the skin has been hardened at the tip of the penis in those who have not been circumcised, or there is an injury or abscess, you must then scrape it off with a sharp instrument, as far as the ligaments are untied, and free the head of the penis from all parts; and if this is a difficult thing to do, you must then scrape it off with a spatula having a pointed edge at the tip of the penis and the scrotum; then separate them carefully, and put in between two small damp linen cloths cooled in cold water.
de la circoncision	Il semblerait que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La circoncision est une opération médicale qui consiste à couper le prépuce (la peau qui recouvre l'extrémité du pénis) pour des raisons religieuses, culturelles ou sanitaires. Voici quelques informations générales sur la circoncision :
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the separation of continuation like other wounds; nonetheless when we do this work of our own will and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say circumcision of their children, for they did not do it in their law, and we have only what we acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and doctors who performed circumcision around one day, with strong forceps, and all a small knife; the knives were so sharp that they had two edges, and perhaps if you cut above it would stay below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now the cut heals, and the pain is doubled, and with the purification which is two days is not assured the point of the member; and with the purification of the wound perhaps escapes the iron, and runs the work, and many times they are born so that there is no need for purification and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done with forceps all the thread of it I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forceps cut equally well above as below.

When you press your hand, cut it evenly in a straight line from tip to base; but the thread should be well tightened around the skin. dou retenement de l’urine	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or intestinal blockage, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention because of the stone which is stuck at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and he should be placed on his back with his feet on the back, and extend his stomach from the part above the back, and restrain the patient's abdomen as much as possible; and then the neck of the bladder is forced out by expression to the stone above, because of which the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe", from which its form: and it should be made of subtle thin silver thread, such as a bird's feather; and it should be one and a half palms long, and delicate at the tip.

Take the double thread, and tie it to the top of a wool or cotton pouch, and put the end of the thread into the catheter; and cut off any surplus cloth and put it right up to the top of the catheter. des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When purulent or bloody matter comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see it distilled in sharp liquids and medicines, so make all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the place is blocked by which the medicine cord is such that it stops the penis well without addition, so that we can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see putting your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the catheter into the moisture, and pull on the string that is in it; if you pull the moisture onto the catheter, and then push hard the string in; if the moisture enters, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle suppository by which we suppurate the bladder: thus is it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of archaic (material), and the head is higher; and below are two breasts where the strings fall; then take a lamb's bladder and put the moisture that you see to suppurate the bladder into it, then tie it between the two breasts with good double thread, and heat the pouch over the fire; then put the head of the catheter in the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has flowed, so that the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make one circle, and pierce it round about; then tie the thread tightly through these holes, then assemble the circle like assembling a roof tile, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	It seems like we've reached the end of this medical text excerpt. The text appears to be describing a medieval medical instrument called a "clistere" or catheter, which was used to drain fluids from the body.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone that is formed from rainwater, and all the signs, and which stone one must operate on by surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign that water has jumped from the bladder similar to water in its subtlety; and I will explain further, and tell the patient to grasp his penis and try many times, and then relax; and there are many such jumps in the foundations; and is light the recovery of children until they have .iiii. years, and it is very grievous in old men, and happens most often in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treating him, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a laxative, so that all the bad blood is drawn out of his intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders in getting at the stone.
