Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall at the touch from top to bottom, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is youthful and completed; and insert it into his fundament, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, guide it down to the neck of the bladder; then press up on your finger, and push it out the farther side where you see the place to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to stretch out his right hand towards the top of the scrotum, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the area where the incision is made. Then I insert the scalpel cutting, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Between those who is between the testicles and the fundament, not in middle but on the side of the left buttock; and be straight above the stone, and your hands be at the fundament, and the shape of the tweezers so that it be large behind, and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, nor too big; by chance the pressure may make the stick which is in the fundament jump out without effort; and know you there are some stones with angles, and edges: if it's grievous to come out; and there are those that are smooth like a bean, and rounded, whose exit is easy.

To that one therefore where there are angles and edges, make the shape larger; and if it doesn't jump out, then you must take hold of the pincers which are like a file at the head, in order to strain the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you put below the instrument with a curved head; and if you can't extract it thus, then enlarge the hole, and if the skin is torn, then bind it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, then push the largest one to the neck of the bladder, then chop above, then pull it out, and the small ones afterwards if there are more.

For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out at once because the place cannot heal; but nonetheless try to draw it out, or cut off with pincers as much as you can draw out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, then bind the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it steady, and put a moist cloth on top of it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water to calm the hot abscess; then raise the patient up onto his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.

Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and ulcers come into the wound and congealments of blood in the bladder, and are held back by these things, preventing the flow of urine which normally comes with it: then cool down your poultice in the wound, and draw out that blood, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and spoil it; then lift the wound up with water and ashes and linen, and help him in every way you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you do to cure him, that you bind his two thighs together, and assemble medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron instrument shaped like this, and with three angled points fixed into a stick:.

de la piere des femmes	This appears to be a new section of text, unrelated to the previous conversation.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the stone is formed in women, and it happens any time, then the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who reveals herself to midwives, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is such that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is such that the stone of the woman lies deeper than the stone of man, therefore it is necessary to make a more profound cut, and there is great fear. And if need arises for you, it is necessary that you take a wise woman and at once find one, and if you do not find her, then do not cast yourself in a subtle art; and have present a good and wise midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you order from the investigation of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to put your hand or foundation and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then bind it under your hand, and recommend that she inserts your hand or holds the patient's left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearances in order to know the exit.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the pain comes back, then apply vitriol paste to the place and hold it for an hour until the pain subsides; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones from humans to aid you in your work; and if the pain returns, and this is due to the artery being cut, then apply powder on the place and the strain of tents and bandages, and do not repeat this again, and leave the stone alone, nor pull it out, lest the patient might die; then treat the wound.

de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The assembled moisture or white secretion, which is under the shell of the egg, that contains the yolk; and it's called "syfac", and sometimes it's properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it might be another egg; and this is the skin of the eggshell between the white syfac that we said; and this can only occur.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of this moisture is so weak that it comes to the eggs, and spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes if it comes from percussion on the groin, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a color declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or aquous white, and so on; and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is of a white color as we have said, then the abscess is reasonable, I say long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the groin, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if he has moisture in the proper fabric, then the abscess is reasonable with a part of the yolk, and because of this we think it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the groin and the white scab, you'll find it quite well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, inspect the surrounding quarter carefully, for what shape it has been before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the pricking, judge of that which is inside. (This sentence seems to be a conclusion or a summary, indicating that one should examine the result of the pricking in order to understand the contents of the egg.)
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be anointed according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then have him sit on his back on something quite high, and put a lot of cloth underneath him; then sit yourself on his left side, and instruct the attendant that he should sit at his right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the cure for the stones; then take the scalpel lightly, and cut the skin of the stones through its length up to the tip, and make the incision entirely straight by cutting the skin of the stones just until the white part appears, and scrape it finely according to our power; then pierce the white part directly with a sharp instrument to a large hole, and extract all the water, and then put your stitches, and sew up the white part upwards; and do not touch the cure for the stones, but only the skin of them; cut entirely or in pieces at once the edge of him finely, that if you do not cut it well and skillfully, the water will come back; and if the stone jumps out during your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the skin of the stones; then join the two leaves of the cure for the stones with a suture, and then treat him as other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the blood corrupted by another disease, it is fitting that you tie the vessels that are suspended, by closing off the hemorrhaging of blood; then cut the kidney away from all the suspensory parts, and extract the blood, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the thigh is assembled into two parts together, know that they are two splints; if you knock the other part so as to equalize it with the first, then bleed it, and put in the wound a moistened wool cloth in rose oil; and put outside another moistened wool cloth in wine and oil, and put on the two limbs, and cover them with doubled cloths, and tie them up above all the bandage that is according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with torn linen according to this shape and have them sewn together in the gusset of the breeches, and one end takes up to the base just to the back, and the other to the part of the knee; and both ends on the two angles, and it is all assembled in a bandage in the buckle of the breeches; and often medicine this splint with cauterization instead of iron surgery, and it is that you take a sharp cauterizing tool, and knock against the skin of the limbs, and be heated as we said, so that the white scab that contains the water is uncovered; if you take the cauterizer according to this shape, and perforate that scab at once, and scrape with this hot cauterizing tool.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And you cover the cautery in all ways that you can, so long as you reach everything; and beware that the fire does not touch the yolk; and know that this work is more safe; and carefully watch for discharging of blood, and beware of the works of cutting; and if anything contrary happens to you, whether it be a chaulm or discharge of blood or another thing, then cure what is causing you trouble, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horror, then administer perforation, as I told you, and know that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the abscess is located, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the lower part up to the entire spatulum wide, and put the perforation very long into the body; and let the hole be large so that all the water flows out; then place cotton on the wound and tie it, and leave for it to flow out the remaining water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the water come out at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument by which one treats the water of dropsy, from which this form comes; and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the water will return, and be gathered after six months or about it, and when it is gathered as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this disease there is great fear and many dispositions, why it seems to me that it is better to let it be; and I will tell you the work and the likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many apostemes come in the body, and indeed in the groin; and it is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known by acidity and corruption that spreads to the testicles, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the flesh; and it does not feel pain, and the abscess is heavy; and perhaps there are heavy, painful, and pus-filled abscesses with a foul color, and sometimes they come from a burst artery, or an inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from a burst artery, it is known by the warm disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fist; and it does not seem right that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from an inflammation of a vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fist; and you can do well to make an incision over this resemblance, and over the other veins; and that you cut the ligament of the testicles, then the seed sac rises up, and the white scrotal skin, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the seed sac.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the boil is already solid with these new hairs, then you must drain the boil and the abscess; and if it is aered at the syphac, or in those things that are inside the blisters, then you must release all of that fluid, and the abscess afterwards.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the child is behind its place, then you must cup it all, and draw out the eye, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your tasks are accomplished, then bind the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then care for it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess surrounded by a wrapping similar to the fig-burst, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient moves grievously when he goes; and the cure for this disease is very similarly fearful as the one before, and nonetheless we will tell you its work, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated throne, then place the suspender of the testicles down to your shoulders, and all the blisters close to the penis, and bind them together tightly; then cut at the scrotum with a sharp-edged knife wide enough to cross over the blisters, so they are uncovered, and then scrape off from each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come out, and tie it again to the other head; then cut in between right through, according to the length of the body, and drain off the corrupt moistors; then treat the wound as with the others or we bleed from above, so that any blister does not burst forth and nourish one of the testicles; for by doing this there is no harm, and if all blisters come out in a vein, it is necessary to cut out the testicles at all the blisters; so that the scrotum may not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the blisters, and they dry up and cannot help each other.
de la routure dou syfac	of the twisting of the joint
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this disease come about by means of the cut that comes from the syphac or through stretching over the belly in the region of the navel, for which the intestines descend into one of the groins; and this rupture is either due to the syphac or due to its excessive extension, and there are these two ways of death by cause: or percussion, or a blow, or vomiting, or the lifting of a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the syphac, are that there are pock marks and pock marks in a long time, and they do not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal right down to the bottom, because the syphac presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a tearing of the joint, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the swelling appears in different forms, just under the skin nearby, and this is because of the exit of the intestine and the body's flesh from the joint.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the joints, and are retained there, and cause great pain to suffer by the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments of iron with vinegar, why it is necessary to be careful not to get burned.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of operating is that you instruct the patient to draw the intestine into his hand from inside the wound if it can enter; then bind a strip around his neck between your hands and lift up the hips. Then incline the back, and cut all the skin over the groin long; then insert within the girdle stitches as needed to open the wound so that the eyes can emerge. Then scrape out the syphac that is under the skin of the groin until the white syphac is uncovered on all sides; then place your two index fingers in what touches the groin, between the white syphac which is under the skin of the egg and between the second syphac, and separate what is behind the egg and between the second syphac. And move your right hand inside the back of the groin, and incline the white syphac to your left hand, and lift up the egg with all its surrounding tissue towards the girdle; and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and release what is tied behind the suture; and inspect with both hands if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around the white syphac; and if you find anything, put it back into the belly under. Then take a needle where there are four thick threads made from ten threads, and insert it in the posterior part of the syphac which is after the skin of the groin; after the girdle, then cut off the ends that appear from the threads as long as there are four threads; then assemble one on top of another like a cross, and bind the syphac with a strong suture of two thicknesses. Then wrap the threads of the sutures around the syphac, and bind them firmly with two thicknesses so that no vessels that nourish them can enter into us, lest an abscess forms there; and put back the suture as before the first long suture of one hand's length. And then leave the syphac which is under the skin of the groin as wide as one finger, and after that all the rest according to the shape that the egg bears; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the groin until it is clean and the sinew and cord are as we said before. Then apply moistened wool in oil and put on the wound, and apply the suture that we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white scar tissue is cauterized that we have said to do after incision, by doubt of bleeding from the wound.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	There often happens this, and let the string hang until it snaps by itself; and if it takes too long to fall, it is razed with hot water, and do what we have said, until it snaps; then heal the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never saw anyone dare to do the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done in such a way as the ramie vine which is wrapped around the bowstring, in the same manner that you tie the vassels, after cutting on them lightly from below; then split it in half, and treat the abscess of those who work at it, until the vassels break; and then cure it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the entrails, as we have said, and opens up the hole; and no strings are to descend into the intestines towards the groin, and if some do descend, it is bad, and mend them at once; and however, if they remain too long in this point, the wound or abscess becomes inflamed, until the intestines come out; and this happens through the stretching of the abscess which is in the entrails, as we have said, for it is stretched, then softened and swollen the hole and opens up; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and this is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the inflamed rupture of the large intestine according to the size of three thumbs; and then extract the entrails which are below the skin next, then take the blade and put it on top of the apparent part of the entrails; and press at the bottom of the belly, then sew up the two visible parts of the entrails on the tip of the blade, and sew one and the other; then extract the tip of the blade, and do not cut the entrails nor stretch out the bowels nor any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the ramie intestine rupture; then heal it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you bind up the boys, instruct the patient to keep the wound free of mud and care for it until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The stitch is constricted and does not show in the rupture, and the cauterizing is more effective in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the intestines
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the intestines becomes softened in some people, because the contents inside are softened, and it can be seen; and when one wants to treat it, one must have the sick person lie on their back, and cut off the softened skin above the natural skin. Then sew together the two lips at a seam, and if you want, sew first the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread hang loose.
dou chastrement	of punishment (or possibly "discipline")
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason it would please me if I did not speak of it at all in this book; and it is necessary only for two ways: one being that the physician knows how to answer questions about the cure when asked, and the other, because we often have need of castrating certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by traction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and during that time; then we take them with your hand, holding them until they are returned to their place and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is necessary that you paint the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and strike up on each cut with a stick, when you have well skinned them; and I leave no pus in the syphac and the subtle syphac which is above the scrotum; and this manner of chastisement is worse than that which is made by attraction, for it happens by chance some thing remains from the testicles, because of which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	The hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermophrodyte is according to two manners among men: the one is that between the two testicles is also open as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in court urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is among women, and has on the elbow as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of a boil and a carbuncle is that you tie the enclosed hairs all together and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine drips through the skin of the groin, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of witchcraft
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is an enclosed boil on the natural part, as long as it is quite ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the boil with tentigene on your hand or fingernails, and tie it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest there come forth bleeding from it, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and for another boil that arises at the mouth of the navel, and apply a poultice, and by chance it bursts forth, and it looks like a cow, and therefore they called it in ancient times "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you perform it, as we have said the treatment, and care for her until she is healed.
de erratique	It seems you're quoting from an old medical text, likely from medieval Europe.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erraticcy is what happens when the nature of the woman is not apparent, or if the womb is small; and it occurs by birth, or by accident through illness that has come to her; or it is caused by a mass of flesh, or a subtle or thick clot, made in front, or on the sides, or underneath, anywhere; and hinders conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers [i.e. menstruation]; and knowledge of this comes from looking at the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is close to appearing, it should be examined by your hands or by a touch.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle clot and it is close to the two kidneys, be quick, and go like this: put your two fingers together, and the woman should lie on her back, spread her legs; then bring the two kidneys into line, as long as the subtle clot is gone, and the swelling will pass; then take linen, soak it in oil, and put it on the place, and bed the woman at home each day, so that she cannot stir.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scab is hard and thick, so it is necessary that you rub with the spatula the part similar to the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is of flesh, suspend it to a vinegar and scrape it; and take on hand medicines to stop blood, such as vitriol, dragon's blood, incense, together with plenty of egg white; then apply a bandage of linen wide, so that the wound cannot close; and thus be long, and then apply a cloth of dry linen; then be cured by other treatments until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes flesh, so it needs to be scraped according to this manner, if it is not enchanted abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an enchanted abscess that is in the marrow, one must not touch with fire.
des emorroides	Voici une traduction de la partie du texte qui parle des émorrhoides :
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Swollen veins are openings of veins from which blood flows freely and habitually, and when the swollen veins are old they become varicose; and we have said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and varicose veins, when they are deep inside the buttocks and cannot be felt by touch, do not receive a cure with an iron instrument.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the opening of the buttocks and can be felt are those which can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, and then heat the hemorrhoid with tongs, and cauterize its roots, and sprinkle on medicines restraining blood, such as aloes and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the belly for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is bleeding from it, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rind and gall and similar things; and then take barley flour, and mix with honey and myrrh, and make into a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he remains still, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him take airsets on the back and under the armpits without hurting them; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has settled down, then treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a head of scabies, so you must cut it out as I said to remove the thistle; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the armpit
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the groin, such as a carbuncle and a suppurating abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary that I say in this book the hot abscess which comes to the groin, which is not among those abscesses that bleed easily; and if you wish to know how to treat iron, see whether the abscess is acute at the beginning of its onset, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to incise, but let it fester as long as the pain is calmed down; and then have the patient sit on a stool, and take two small stools for them to lean against, and support their back and bring their feet to the outer part of the leg; and have their thighs spread out, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then suck out the pus towards the right side, and introduce the instrument by which one works on the mouth of the groin, from which this form comes next; and it is necessary that when you see bring in this instrument, that you insert the first part into the depth to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters inside the instrument does not come more deeply than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not bother them; and it is necessary to put the cone of the instrument above, and to temper the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open and you make it soft with your hand, then you must cover at the head, at the place of the sputum; and when the boil is empty, you must put in the wound moist tents made in rose oil, or in green verdant oil; put the tent far from the wound to the bottom of the gauze, and put over the gauze and on the fold linen damp in water or beets that have been cooked; then cure it after 2 days of ointment having occurred according to them, until you are clean; and sometimes lift the gauze and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and Aristolochia longa that have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is joined in the gauze, you must be careful not to cook with iron, but heal it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Il semble que vous ayez demandé un texte médical ancien qui traite de la gynécologie et de la obstétrique. Le texte que j'ai traduit précédemment était probablement une section sur les affections de la peau, mais maintenant vous me demandez de traiter du sujet plus spécifique de l'enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary for the midwife to know the figure of natural childbirth and its signs; that is when you see the woman advance downward, and desire to smell the air: then the child hastens to issue forth quickly; therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is under her head, and the secondine with it. And when you see these signs, it is necessary to press her belly slightly so that the child issues quickly; for when it rises up on its head, the secondine comes with it, and the mother is freed of her superfluities by good cleaning; and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	Because it sometimes comes out its feet, and issues forth from the body or head, and hands, or comes up on her belly, or side, and is turned by chance over her neck, and by other bad shapes; so it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out over its head in a natural birth, and the woman gives birth easily, and the virtue of her is weak, let her sit on a chair, or women hold her; and anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then put the ball (or dough?) between her lips, in the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and tear the perineum, and prick at its edge until the moisture that is inside comes out; and grasp the woman's belly as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, so it is necessary to enema the woman with fenugreek mucilage in sesame oil; then have her grasp and strain of condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus now the child goes.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, so it is necessary that you reset them gently tap by tap; and if they cannot enter, so put the woman on the stool, and lift her feet high; then lower the stool to the ground, and keep hold of the woman, so that she does not jump up; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, so prick the hands with the knife that is placed before, and extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the baby comes out onto its feet, you should push it up; and then turn it little by little, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it jumps up to the knees, you should tell it to stay still, and cause it to be stunned with conditio; if it jumps further, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he does not jump up as we have said, then turn it a little by little until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For at that time it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then say to take muscilage from almonds, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put the woman's natural substance inside and on top of this ointment, then make her sit in a warm bed down to the hips; and when it is moistened below, then tie the girdle of myrrh around her, and put it under, and let it stay an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then cause her to be stunned and restrain her mouth and nose, and lightly touch her belly, for the baby now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the exit of a child from its thigh (or legs).
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the baby comes in this form, so put it on your hands and hold it pok and pok; then be careful on its neck, and let the feet hang down, and be on the floor; and fold its hands pok and pok, and then take its hands on the belly, and remove the pillows underneath, until it is ready to come up; and if the baby doesn't fall, take its feet and straighten them out, then lift the belly up, then put your hands in; and hold the baby pok and pok; and instruct the woman to take a hold of herself until the baby comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the exit of the child which comes out with a hand on the side.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It becomes necessary to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, have her lie on the bed, and lift her legs straight; then administer the medicament that I mentioned; and if she does not give birth, have her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and deliver the baby in its natural form, and have it cry out, and instruct the woman to take hold of herself until the baby comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of a child on its neck, and has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the doctor takes his hand, then turns it slowly and carefully, and stretches it lightly; and when it is even, so he puts on the natural medicated oil of althea and olive, as we have said, then instructs her to move slowly and slowly; and when you have done this, have her sit on a stool, and instructs her to grasp it; and has her stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	by the same method for both wrists.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner in the second birth, so the midwife strikes the second child at the finger, until the moisture is empty; and if the afterbirth hangs on her face and on her neck, so she strikes from the mouth, so that it does not remain, and let out the afterbirth; then insert the child inside, as much as it is necessary, and command the woman to grasp it once: then it will go lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the birth of twins (this text seems to be a medieval medical manual, specifically discussing methods for delivering babies in a somewhat gruesome manner)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and never more than three or four at once; and this is not an uncommon thing, it happens often enough.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange things, and do not live, if they have a name; I know them to be multiplicity, and they are severed by the spleen that divides them, which is tied to the belly; and sometimes they issue forth as naturally as eggs from a hen, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue grievously, then the treatment should be as we have said, and the spleen should be subtle, and perform quickly and lightly what it does; and do thusly as it moves towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the belly in the first month or second or third or fourth or fifth or sixth or seventh, or more than that up to fifteen, and they take all shape like an infant by the measure of their size, and it is necessary for the spleen to know everything about them, because perhaps a similar thing has happened; so do according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	of the stillborn child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the deceased or unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to operate by hand; then you must know if the woman is in good health, and has no accident, or she fears death; then the woman should be supported on her back, and her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and give the mother of II parts, or tie her to bed so that she is not treated with the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the mare with moistened oils mixed with muscillaige of aloes and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint the hands of the mare with these oils and these mixtures; then put them into the mare lightly, then look where the ondines are placed that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is apparent it will descend over its head; so stick the ondines in her eyes or in her neck or in her mouth or in her palate or below the beard or in the forehead or near the ribs or in the places, and if the descent is on the feet, then stick or prick them and the opposite sides; and you must give the ondine to her right hand, and put the corbeure between her left arm and her shoulder, and insert the ondine into any of these places that we have said, until it comes to an empty thing; and this is the shape of the ondine:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Next to the other wound, or the third if you have need of it, so that the extractions be equal; and then hold them equally in moving from one side and to the other, so that they may issue out, and the wounds may be sown with stitches to hold them, as is this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, anoint the ball with some of his oils from the deer, and insert them in that part, and pull out the other part; and if there remains nothing, then place this wound or move it to a higher position, and do so until all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be returned due to stricture, then you must wrap over with a cloth until it all comes out; then stitch in the joint of the sole or at the ankle, and thus you must do also on the other hand, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it has a sharp point assembled at birth, you should insert the spatula of the spine between your fingers, make the head and extract the bone; or use the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and do the same for the child who naturally has a large head; and then draw out the bones with forceps, and if the bone jumps out and it strains at the forceps, split it so that the moisture can come out; and if it cannot come out, break it in pieces at the joint where you can; and if it is inflamed on the belly or under the ribs, you should prick through until the moisture drains.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the baby is on its feet, and the descent is easy, and the approach to the mouth of the womb is light; (i.e. an indication that delivery is imminent and may proceed normally)
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is inflamed in the belly or at the chest, you should extract it with the drapeil enveloped over the hand; and cut the belly or chest until the moisture that is there drains; and if the other members are broken off, and the head remains, you should bind a bandage to the arm from the shoulder down, and draw it up to the mouth of the navel; then insert the finger or two, and draw it out; and if the mouth of the navel is shrunk because of hot abscess that has come there, you should not struggle with it, but rather moisten and anoint things; and apply ointments and thus in a softening and soothing way.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the hernia is on his side, and you can place it even, do as we have said for a living child; and if you cannot, then cut it through with pieces, and leave nothing of the skin.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, do as we have said for cold abscesses that come in the groin; and if there is discharge of blood coming, it should be put in clean water tightly tied, and do other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then she covered one other on top of that one, and rejected the death of the others; (i.e. the woman's uterus contained two fetuses, but only one was stillborn, while the other fetus was viable)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, it came out some swellings in the mouth, and swelled so much that it opened up, and began to rot; (i.e. the stillborn fetus was surrounded by a foul-smelling, decomposing tissue)
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound; (i.e. despite my best efforts, I was unable to properly sew up or close the incision site)
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong ointment of attraction, and came out a bone, and after some days, another one; (i.e. the decomposing tissue and bones were slowly being released from the woman's body)
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because in that belly there is no bone; (i.e. despite my initial assumption that the swelling contained bones, it turned out to be a type of soft tissue or membrane)
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child. (i.e. I mistakenly believed that the hard, calcified material was the remains of a stillborn fetus)
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I closed the wound, and drew in several bones, until the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived long in this way, and so it was always a little better from the start; and I have not forgotten this chapter, unless because when the master finds an unusual thing, he does not know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the womb to its place. (i.e. a conclusion to the text, indicating that the discussion about childbirth and the uterus is now complete)
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, to which we owe the books; and to two turnings at two hands of the two links. (i.e. a reference to the physical characteristics or design of some tool or instrument used in bookmaking)
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horn should be more subtle than the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and its mouth should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the wood one palm and a half long; and between the two loops there should be two insertions of the same wood, which are firmly inserted in each, half a palm long or a little more; and these two inserts are placed in the mouth of the groin to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	A different form, more subtle and lighter in shape, is made of ebony wood or boxwood, according to the shape of pincers; and has two handles, just as you see, a palm's length long, and two fingers wide; and when you see opening the wound with the entire instrument, so sit the woman on a bed, her feet spread out and her legs open; then insert the two handles inserted together into the wound, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand over the entire instrument, as you have done equally with the pincers, according to the size that you see opening the mouth of the wound, until the woman has done what she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.
