These instruments are all perfected, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the midwives have prepared them, then the work is done more quickly, and higher in value to men for their quantity. (i.e. a conclusion that emphasizes the importance and value of these instruments in the practice of midwifery)
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	And do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for its necessity is not excusable. (i.e. a reminder to always be prepared and equipped with the necessary tools and instruments in order to properly perform one's duties)
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then make her sneeze with condise, and hold your hands on the mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take I a hot coal, and make a hole or cover on it, and put herbs which can open the mouth of the sore, such as calamine, rue, anise, chamomile, cassaliaigne, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, be cooked or put in water over the fire; then take a thread or hole from the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the sore, and make it steam so that the vapors come inside the sore; then let it sweat, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the afterbirth comes out quickly. (i.e. an expression of success or completion, indicating that the delivery has gone smoothly)
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not completely healed, instruct the girl to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or with muskallage of althea, and then put it in nature, and look for the second line; and when she has found it, take it and stretch it a little bit straightly, so that the sore does not crack on extraction; but it must be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pulled out; and it will come out and heal itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the uterus is constricted, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation of herbs; and if she does not respond to all that we have said, beware lest you proceed hastily; but it behooves those who are at the mouth of the uterus, that you bind it to the navel of the woman, then clisterize with tetrafarmacous ointment; so she may come out and be placed back, and be well again; but nonetheless, when she purges thus, a foul odor comes to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is thus fitting to make fumigations that are suitable for this: no one of the ancients has tried fumigation with lettuce and dried figs. (i.e. a reference to an ancient medical practice or remedy, using fumigation as a means of treating the woman)
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at the retention of flowers and afterbirth is thus: (i.e. a description of how to use an instrument or tool to create a type of vapor or fume that can be used in conjunction with herbal remedies)
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be observed that it resembles a girdle, and one puts the head in a subtle nature, and the hives wide on the fire; and there are fumigations above the coals, and the lice until they are consumed, and then another starts again.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament (i.e. a term used to describe a medical procedure or treatment, likely referring to piercing or incising the perineal area)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather it is stopped by a fine syphac: so therefore at the bath, that it pierce this syphac to its due, and does not pierce with a spatulated point, and secure the ligature so that it does not touch; then put on wet linen in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put or make a hole with a piece of linen, and let the hands remain for days, and be removed when the child wants to go to the chambers (i.e. the perineal area may need further treatment and care after childbirth)
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And whenever this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or swelling, it is fitting to cover that sudden stoppage: if it is cured, as we have said of the piece of linen. (i.e. a description of how to care for and treat any unexpected complications or obstructions that may arise during childbirth)
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament (i.e. a medical condition where an abnormal connection or passageway forms between the skin and the rectum, causing leakage or discharge)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that come from under the fundament are nodation, and grow larger when they come from below the fundament outward, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodation is old, it works, and also makes moist abscesses or fine boils, and sometimes these fistulas disappear; and are known by this that they spit up or vomit blood or mucus when the patient does a purge, and by chance spit out a worm.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if you have fistulas that perforate just to the bladder, and just to half of the penis, and reach just to the junction of the navel and just to the knee. (i.e. a description of the extent or severity of the fistula)
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus you know the fistula is persistent at the fundament and not persistent: and it is that you prick your middle finger or fundament, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no turnings.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is turnings, then I insert a thin tent of cloth or the hair of a horse, as far as you feel the tent or the hair at your fingertip; and if you don't feel it, and it does not come out with discharge, windiness, or worm, just as we have said: know that it is not piercing; if you are hasty to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has pierced just up to the bladder or just up to the urethra channel, then it lets out urine and cannot be healed with medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is piercing just to the joint of the thigh, then the tent comes out to its place; if there is no turnings and the inflammation of pain around, it is that it is going away by itself, and does not require medicine or ointment; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure strong except surgery, and the vanity of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not yet healed and is not yet old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it lies between your hands on his back; and he lifts up his legs to his hips, and has his hips inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of tin, or of lead if it has tortuosity, so long as you know where the tent comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your middle finger, and if you sense that the tent has pierced it; and is discovered where you feel between your thumb the skin or flesh, then know that it is healed; if not I trouble with it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says that one can well heal some, but it is rare; and the aid that we do there, if it is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and put it all hot in the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that those flesh marks are seared, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then cure with moist tents in butter, as long as those flesh marks come out, then cure with ointment anointing flesh and joining.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus cleansed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this, otherwise cannot be cleansed; and the probe enters, and does not pierce just to the bottom which is on the foundation, and between the probe and the boil there is a thick covering of flesh or of pus, and you see the fistula where the covering touches the core; if you cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push it forward before the boil, and then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the boil; and the boil will be delivered, and will dry up; then scrape away those blackened pieces that resemble a bird's feather, and let none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain comes back to you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or a hot medicament.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery puts two things together: that is to say, the charring of those blackened pieces, and the drying up of blood and moisture; then treat boils moist with butter or broths made from cheese, until the spot discharges pus, and then send out the charred pieces in the pus; then treat the wound with ointments drawing out hard flesh, and they are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the bottom of the fundament, and is far from the body, then plug it with your finger or fundament, and investigate inside.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tumor, and between two is the cloth or the syphac or char, where it is close to piercing, so there are no fires but a view of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners: or you cauterize him as we have said, or you cut him just to the bottom, or if you can see I put tents and cure as first; and do not go too deep at first, that you do not cut the container which holds the foundation, and come the evacuations by the sense of volition; then cure it, as we have said; by chance it will be cured, or you remove that cover and clean it since it is cut close to the foundation, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then cleanse that charred flesh which is in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part above the foundation: if it were a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And any time a fistula is made in this manner: and it is when you probe the tent in the fistula, and it is on one side near the foundation next to the skin above, then take a thorned tent at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and I put one twisted thread in two, and plug the needle into all the thread in the fistula as far as its head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then draw out the string of that thorned tent, thus as you probe your finger or foundation; and pull the top of the string, and join the two ends together, and hold one against the other, and let it stay for a day or two; and hold it again, until the string dries these threads that are between the two, and they close; then cure the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to pierce the binding that has been sewn up too deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spine needle from which the fistula is made is very sharp on one side and tapered; and on the other side not, because of which those things are not pierced that should not be pierced, as you see here:
des emorroydes	nerves.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emperydes are according to two manners: or they are inside the fundament, just like grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in cortex already blood, and there is one or more, and are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those which are outside so have much moisture, and immediately become a drop of clear water or a drop of blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament, you command the patient to urinate so that the fundament may issue forth, and that they may see the strings; if it is urgent, and you take with tweezers, or hold it at your nail, then cut in their roots; and if the surgeon cannot hold because of their moistors, you take them on a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamelot; and you pull them out to your hands, then cut them, and powder over hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them just as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then you cure with other cures until they be sane; and if the fundament cannot issue, you catheterize the patient with a catheter biting and harsh to wash what is inside the fundament, so that it may issue clearly; since the patient feels pain, and the string are forth from the fundament, it is the easy cure; and is that you take them at your nail or with tweezers, and cut them, then you cure just as we have said, until they be sane, and that he fear not the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you bring the suture according to this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread around the needle, so that it be doubled; and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one end to let out the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation a damp cloth in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave him until they stop bleeding, and when they will have stopped, so cure them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the healing of the anus or fundament.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often times there is a healing of the anus in the intestines, and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you clean the point of a splinter or at your nail the skin above it, which does not let it moisten; then cure him until he is sound as it is necessary; and if he cannot be healed, so start again to scrape more strongly than before, until he heals thoroughly, and is skinned over; then cure him until he is healed.
dou fremit	of hemorrhoids.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Anter the body is a small false appearance, and it goes deep inside; and sometimes the frost finds it, and you sense it just like the dead feel numbness, and it comes into all the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a stick from an owl's feather, or a strong duck's quill, and place that stick on the numbness, until the red circles appear all around it; then turn your hand to hold the whole stick so as to cover all of the numbness, and push it deep in, and pull out the numbness from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see [fit], then make it with a wire of iron or steel in this shape, and be thin under and twisted above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and squeeze it And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is written in the book of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the cathartic.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times one makes a cathartic of silver or lead, or melted tin or alloyed metal; and at times one makes these instruments small and large, according to the shape in which they are made.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, the ones that are made for the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the cathartic, big or small, is above wide, or the belly is joined in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it has an obstruction or the belly is bound together, just as you see, and the head is pierced from inside; and it has two holes on one side, and one on the other, and there are medicines in a animal skin or parchment that have been put into the belly and pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there is a space of an eighth part; then insert a strong thread of twisted yarn in X shape or knot around it, and bind the belly together as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie up the instrument in front with a strong thread; and that's how you make the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or marrow of egg or similar thing, then put it on lightly; then compress the minister to both hands together until it is all swollen, then extract the blister, and lift the patient's legs high and have them hang from the bed, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it be for as long as it can; and if they sleep one night altogether, so it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catharticize him in the sickness of intestinal obstruction, and the medicine comes out quickly, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, let the blister be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle blister on which the skin is held tight:
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of the treatments of hands and of medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things through which wounds are made are by striking with stone, and cutting with sword and knife or lance or club or arrow or similar thing; or those that are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt lightly of hot abscess: so make it heal quickly with cephalic salve just in case there is bleeding from the wound, and the salve is applied to the contrary part of the injured area; and instruct the patient to drink wine and eat thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, let the patient eat less meat, and do not drink wine, nor chew any fat; and put over the wound, if a hot abscess comes, moistened cotton in rose oil alone, or in stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder that I will say about later; and if the burn has moved it, then put some ointments over it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword or similar things, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then stitch them together with sutures, just as I will say about belly wounds, in the chapter of suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and raw, and holds together only by a thin thread, cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as roasted testes and barley bread, also like fowls, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a skin corruption, and it is not to the bone, cut out all the corruption, and wash away; then cure him; and if there are arteries in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: you put on this powder which heals even when the air has spoiled it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of this powder is: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of living alum, and grind it finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, so that it adheres well and joins with all its blood; and then tie it well, and let it be without untying, if it does not swell; for one does not remove medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times we make this with calamine alone, when we do not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but only when the air has spoiled the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, so much in itself, do not put on this powder at all; but apply some digested ointments or hair made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until it discharges pus; then cure him with other cures until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break in the bone comes with the wound and it is small, so extract it with subtle forceps; and I will tell you of breaks of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is an abscess, so there is no other cause except to let the cure be and not put anything restraining on it, for it hurts abscesses and makes them recede; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of abscesses is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be the medicine soft, such as hawthorn laved in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucubut laved also in sweet water, and other powdered herbs according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and tie with bandages, and treat it as long as it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and high and full of pus, then pierce it or lower part; and if the artery is cut, and a flow of blood comes out, then stop it, close it, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conduit is kept so that the flesh goes, then cover the jugular on the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put back according to its natural shape; and then tie it carefully, and leave it for some days, and then cure with ointments of stale fat until it is healed; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, then search for it; and if there are pieces of bone, then extract all that you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound is mature, and is discharged and closed its issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of a spear or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, see if there is windiness emanating from the wound, which would indicate that the patient has been pierced: you will then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it still bleeds its whole blood, do not put powder in the wound at the first hour, nor bind it so tightly that the blood cannot ooze out and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but instead put on attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient sleep on top of the wound for three days, or four, or more; the patient will not get spasms, nor bad trembling from the heart, nor strainings emanating from it; and when you see good dispositions, you will know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat then the abscess and other treatments, as long as it is cleansed; and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is an ulcer; thus treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or on the back, then treat the part that is in front; if it is large, by stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it has pieces broken off in the bone, and it has splinters, then clean the wound, and take out foreign things if they are dislodged; and if they are not dislodged, let the wound become infected, so that the extractions will be easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, make judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from dislocation of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the abdomen are great and medium and small; from the large wound, intestines or the membranes of the intestines sometimes burst forth, because of their entry; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, therefore we insert the intestines more gently, if they are not inserted hot into hot; because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, so that they enter more gently, and therefore a middle-sized wound is better, so that you should carefully move the intestine to its place rather than the other two. And know that the rupture of the abdomen occurs in four ways: two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body, and two other stitches proper are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more suitable with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines has escaped, and a simple thing needs to be done, it can be done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a piece of linen in hot water only, or cook it in hot water with cinnamon and cypress, and spike, and rise the intestine until the inflammation is removed; and once you have done this, restrain it, and be careful that it does not become swollen to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the inflammation depart, if you moisten the intestine in water or wine and have herbs cooked, because through them the entrance is opened to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with an instrument that we use to lance abscesses; and the first treatment is careful not to cut the intestines, for none of us should cut without great necessity being there; and this is the instrument to split it: cut inside in the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have burst forth, so place it back again in its proper natural form, if you are able to do so, for this is advantageous.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part under the belly, then you must have the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part under the belly, so place the head and chest higher than the other parts; and similarly if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, so place what I say in greater and lesser wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put on the dressing that suits you, and then have the patient's minister take hold of the whole routure with his hand, and bring together the lips; and this is the common way of suturing, and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, and leave the head of the wound about two fingers' breadth apart, and insert a needle where there is good thread; and pierce the four keys of the skin with the two keys of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce through from that part, and bring together the two heads of the siphac in one assembly; then take hold of a double thread around the needle on both sides, then bring together the two lips of the wound properly, and leave about two fingers' breadth apart, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you made the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to how many needles you need, until all the wound is bound up; and let the needles be neither too fine nor too coarse, for fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot well enter: for that reason they should be medium-sized; and it does not matter to thrust the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound in front of the suturing; then cut off the heads of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or cloths over the heads of the needles for a more convenient tie, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this way of suture with needles is more advisable in small wounds, for it suffices to use one needle or two; the second suturing is common, and it is that you bring together the four keys of the skin and the four keys of the siphac together into a needle where there is strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these keys all four together, then take out the needle from the part where you began in the manner in which one sews dresses; and leave about the breadth of a little thumb between each suturing; this suturing is known to men, and I sewed up a wound that belonged to a man whose belly was wounded with a knife, which wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines were well two palms long, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to him the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up just in time for 15 days, and he healed, and was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where there was none to be found, nor any medicine; and I placed clean cotton on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and push it from the outside part just to the inside; when it has pierced in right through right, so place the thread or suture where you have pushed in the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside just to the outside; and the understanding of this suture is that you sew as the tinkerers do their pelts, and leave once the thread on one part, and take it up again on the other, until the suturing is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which the Greeks say properly, is such as someone does, who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the heads of the needle to the other head, in this way: place a needle or head of the thread close by, and make it pierce that point alone, and leave the two heads of the needle; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part just up to the inside part, at the two heads of the needle; then make one and the other pierce from the outside part just up to the inside part, in two other eyes of the thread that are on the other side; and this is the more correct manner of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this saying, and some attest it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one should push one needle from one part, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when a tear occurs in the belly, then the sewing is more difficult than at other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the burn has changed it, then replace the intestine and the skin; then put on powdering charcoal dust, and if the burn has changed it, put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and cleanse the stitches, and sew the gauze, and the thread; then heal the wound just as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on old cotton, and move it 2 times a day, until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of another medicine in many simple dispositions of wounds; and if you doubt that the wound will bring on common infection of the principal members, it is necessary that you dip lightweight linen in tempered hot oil or in rosed oil, and place it around the joints and under the shoulders; and if it feels pain or foulness in the belly, and this often happens, then cleanse with black wine decoction, and similarly if the foulness comes just to the intestine; and perforate inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is more likely to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines that are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and it is because of the plantness of the veins that they are in, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approaching of its nature to the gall.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon springs out of the wound, put it back in the same way as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, you must tie up the part that is black so that blood does not flow from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the tendon, and hang the two ends down from the lower part of the wound until the tendon falls out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, one can restore it in certain men, because I have seen that a man was wounded with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and was sewn up and became a fistula, and from it there were discharges and windiness; I applied treatment to it according to what I knew, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the hole closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sew it up, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his belly; and there was no evil, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and certain experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestines, he should be tied in this manner: take linen strips from large loaves, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the linen strip has opened the mouth, put it over the two lips so they hold together; and then knock the head with the end of the linen strip, and that holds so well that he cannot untie it, then put another linen strip after in this same manner until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That linen strip is inserted in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this thread of intestine that has been well stripped, and then bind it to the head of this thread with a thin linen thread twisted together; then thread the thread through the needle and sew up the intestine, and wind it around the seam; and as for the stitching with linen strips, that is no different than by faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, there is no remedy or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of an ulcer or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it festers, is called universally "fistula", and likewise when it breaks out and runs over.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its greenish nodation rough and white, or where one does not feel pain, and it is also running like the plumage of a bird; and sometimes clear pus flows from it, and at other times thick; sometimes little, and at other times enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that any wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it can only be due to one of the nine causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and on the edges, that does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is corrupted, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because of the property in the region is slow digestion, and late healing, and it flees by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I tell you the treatment for fistula which is done by hand's work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and also in such a place as comes to the principal property of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of difficult healing, and there is no choice but to cut, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come exactly to the place I said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it know, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, then probe it; and if the fistula is twisted, then seek with a subtle tent of cloth, for cloth bends easily around twisting; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings, for moisture quickly passes from one opening to another, and purifies it; then probe again with your skill to see if there is bone or nerve, and is deep in position, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressing my hand, and where he feels it; and once you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from a jointure, or from a nerve, or from an artery or vein, or in any of the places I told you, then cut according to what I told you, and remove the putridity and corrupt flesh that are inside; and then heal it until it is whole, and if the fistula is well deep in the right place, then you must cut further, as long as you can, then insert moist tents in medicinal water, and push them just up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluousness that remains at the bottom; and then put on poultices with fresh healthy flesh, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by these means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not strike or harm the main members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then wash it thoroughly until all corruption is removed, then treat with ointments that bring healing to the flesh so long as you are cured; and if he is not cured, and returns to its former state, know that you have not gone deep enough: if you expose and scrape thoroughly until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore it [to its proper place]; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot come to it: if there is no other remedy than to let it go according to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pincers, then take it out with the proper instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, don't leave any behind; and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no error or fear, then cut and scrape through flesh and bone, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put a thing that causes purging on the wound; and let it stay until the place is rotten around the bones; and then they will have the bones more easily; and if it's a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, so that only the corruption remains as long as the blackness is entirely removed, then close the wound; and if there is a great part of the corrupted matter, and comes just to the edge of the bone; you will need to scrape and clean all up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is closed; and I will tell you about an abscess that happened in a man's leg, so that you take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg due to something that came from within the body, so much so that the matter came into the leg and he was afflicted with a large abscess; but there was no opening for it outside; however, the doctors worked on it so much above that they opened the abscess, and there flowed out much matter, and it became an abscess, and many channels appeared through which all of the body's moisture and heat were flowing; and many doctors put medicine around him for two years, and not a wise person in the art of healing knew what to do with him until I was called to see him, and his leg, and the medicines by which they were treating him, and the matter that flowed out through the channels, which had grown large in the body; and the young man's skin became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these depressions, and then searched all the depressions, and found that some were facing each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and made an incision in one of the depressions until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it to be corrupted and pierced, and the corruption had reached as far as the bone inside; I cleaned out what appeared of the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption than what I had removed; and I began to treat the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but could not join it together; and then I re-entered, and found the bone just as before, and discovered that the corruption continued in the bone, and cleaned it out, and then removed it, and leaned forward to join the place back together; but I couldn't do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and freed it all the way up to its base, then restored it with medicines; and it healed quickly and was joined together quickly, and there was no need to re-enter the work except for the patient's weakness, which could not endure, and because of the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation of blood it often bled profusely, but it was entirely cured, and in place of the bone there grew a hard skin, and it was of good disposition and had no harm nor contrary effect at all, neither in growing nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be treated in this manner: take one thread and bind it at the top of the bone which shows, and instruct someone to stretch it up; and take another thread of linen thicker than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone, and bind the ends so that you draw out the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see that it will heal, without hurting the flesh; and put a poultice or a wooden splint under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and it must be left to heal as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and then heal again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.
