And if the bone is corrupted and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, then uncover the flesh entirely; then place a red-hot iron underneath, and then weave a thread from one part to another where the corruption is, and be sure that the thread is long enough to cover the entire length of the corruption as we have said. And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint and sew up the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is between the two joints, then there's no other way but to cut it. And if the corruption is in the wrist or in the ankle of the hand or foot, then that thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire about this corrosion how it will open up; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or the nerve get in your way. And know that there are many instruments for cutting into bones according to the size of the bone and its appearance, thickness, length, and thinness, and hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work. And know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; so think about the instrument that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	from fire;
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulders may be damaged either from within or from without; and when you have medicated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then you must cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes through death or the malice, which is greater, from the defect of the member; and the signs are such that the member becomes black, so that it seems burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption spreads from member to member, and takes over all the body; if you do not hasten to cover it up, and it comes from a blow by some venomous beasts, as scorpion of the sea and viper and similar things, then if the corrosion is on the head of the thumb, cut off that hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut off at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come as far as the arm; and if it comes on the arm, then cut off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there's no other remedy than by the quantity of its virtue; and do in this manner when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the second joint; and if it comes on the foot, then cut off the entire foot; and if it rises up into the leg, then cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, then there's no other remedy but that the patient dies; and the manner of cutting or searing the member is such that you tie it over and under, and stretch out one servant down below, and another servant up above, and you release the flesh between the two straps a little wide, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut or cauterize, and put a linen cloth on either side, so that the sear does not touch the healthy place, and other lesion and abscess will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if hemorrhage comes from the blood when you work, then cauterize the place immediately, or put on some constricting powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the hurt member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed. And I will tell you what happened to my own son: there came a black spot that seemed like coal of fire, and that corrosion first appeared in his toe between the two bones, until it consumed the entire toe; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cauterize the toe, and was healed. And long afterwards the corrosion returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things reactive after the cleansing of the flesh, and the corrosion could not cease; and he asked that I cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of reverberating the matter; and I also doubted that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became despairing altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cauterize his hand, and was healed. And I have not told this tale except because it is done otherwise when one needs it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in the fatty part, and it stays so long that it makes a large gathering of flesh; and then they rot and break through, and the flesh bursts, and leaves the place empty, just like watered wine vessels; and the skin which is above is just as subtle as delicate cloth, and does not spread to the bone or to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain", and it is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone in depth, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is like this: you should cut off that skin all around, and just as it is subtle, just like delicate cloth; and one should not treat it because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have suspicion that the skin is corrupting, and the corruption is not in depth, and the skin is thick with flesh, then cut it off with a cauterization thus: look to see if the breast is large, and the abscess which is inside has a foul odor, then cauterize with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take ash, oil, and lapis lazuli, equally, and put the skin in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes just as thick as honey; and then take some of it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and cauterize the breast, and plug the abscess; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the foul odor is removed; and sometimes a cauterization of ashes' water is done, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ash from grapevine wood, and pour water over it, then let it drip, and cauterize with it, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ashes' water, then cauterize with water and honey, or there is a pinch of lapis lazuli added; or you cauterize with honey and sweet wine, which has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the abscess boil over; and when you have done this, and you have suspicion that the breast is well cleansed, then cauterize with it what causes flesh to grow in it, and it is that you take diaphanit plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you cauterize with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have said about treating ointments; and if the abscess of the breast is small, and the cannula of the cauterization cannot enter it, then enlarge it with a pin a little bit, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, as long as it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave just the place where the cauterization can enter, and if the abscess that pours pus is above, then cut or lower it to where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bow is in depth, one does not let it sprout with hair; and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare in such a manner that the bow goes to the lowest place it is, for when the bow is deep, one does not let it sprout with hair and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare in this way: that the bow goes slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and sew up the linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut at a strong point the hole of the breast where it is more open than before, then anoint with soft ointment on the other cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole of the wound to loosen the bow, and do not remove the large cloth outside that one must keep for many days; and the one that is on the hole of the breast, take often to remove the bow, and know what comes out from the bow, if it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that runs on the hole of the wound, then know that the wound is cured already, and approach the health; and then loosen it in the morning, or the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast pours forth bad blood after many days, know that the breast has not hardened.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons have coursed after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the patient is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds take a long time to heal with scar tissue, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food jumps out of the chest after many days, know that the heart is not well; and if the heart takes a long time to mend and becomes inflamed, use medicinal ointments which are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphanous ointment, because it contains a great part of vinegar, and this is the last medicine; take diaphanous ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the ashes of old wine equal in substance; then stew it and use it; and also do the same thing with thickened honey, when diaphanous ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then bind it in a cloth, and apply it to the chest, and sometimes administer aromatic herbs, and roots of the celestial lily, which is also like flour from vegetables and centaury; and use simple or compound medicines: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption has gone deep, and made impression in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the sinews; if you do the cure of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the aposteme of an ulcer.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the fold of the hand or foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it grows old and one does not take care of it, then the abscess becomes foul and bursts and spews pus as long as it runs the root of the boil, and sometimes runs all the way out; and comes corrosion just to the bone, so that there is a stinking pain, and the skin of the toe is wide open, and the color is putrid.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must take a hot iron to scald all the excess that remains of the boil, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a very great aid if the bone is sound and the boil is healthy; and if the boil bursts into the flesh, begins to prick and wound it, then you must put the hot iron on the boil that pricks the flesh, push it up, and scald that subtle flesh delicately and lightly, and apply the remaining flesh medicines that burn and corrode in order to remove everything; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it out and remove the dead flesh, for as long as the corrupted bone remains inside, it will not heal; and if you see that the two bones are corrupting, then cut them apart in the same way as was said before, then cure them until they are healed; and if it is hardened and swollen, and hurts a lot, then you must first drain it; then cut the flesh around the abscess from a diagonal cut above, and take care that the cut does not reach the skin beneath the abscess, for the patient would feel too great pain; and if it happens, put something on top to calm it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the earache of the hand ( possibly a reference to a specific medical condition).
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The joints that are born in some men's hands by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a place where they have bones, and sometimes there is an ulcer, and occasionally they occur in the root of the joint, or the birth is in one of the bones of the joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with some defect in the joint of the elbow does not move it, and he who is born with a deformity at the joint of the elbow, by chance moves it; the length of the one who is fat is light, similarly: you should cut into its root from a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who arises at the root of the joint is difficult to cure, so you should take care not to cut into it too deeply.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born with or has a growth on the backside of the bone, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh up to the bone first, then cut the bone into a thread suitable for this, then cure it until it becomes sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes on the hand together with others comes from birth, or from a blow, or from being burned by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the seam, so that it heals and mends according to its natural shape; then place between two tents or damp cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together; or you place between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is healed, as is proper.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swelling comes to any of his hands with the palm, then cut out that swelling in the manner that is necessary.
des vils	of evils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Flesh boils are large swollen things full of melancholy humors that come to many parts of the body; and they occur more often in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer them sometimes a purging of gall, and then cleanse them with the lily of the valley (a plant-based remedy).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron (injury) is in two manners: one is to cut them, and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and let it all drain.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is in this manner: raise the leg with a hot iron very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned, then strain the patient's leg from above the knee to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or in two places, or in three, with a large cut, then lift and draw out the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can suffer; and then bind it, and instruct him that he should take on nourishing foods of cold black broth; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The wound's healing is according to this manner: raise the patient's leg if there are many hairs on it, then put it in a bath, and with hot water as sharp as possible until the veins swell, and become red; and if you do not have a bathing place, heat it by the fire, and then apply the needle's point at the vein's edge near the knee, or under the ankle; then sew up the skin to the edge, and peel off the vein from each side, so that when you touch it you can feel it; and it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then place the thread underneath, so that it rises out of the skin, and then sew up lightly, then apply to another needle's point above III times; then peel off the skin on top of the vein until you feel it, then raise the thread, as you have done, and sew up to another needle, as you did first; then apply another size or more if needed, then raise, and sew at the foot's tip, then pull and raise just to the second needle; then draw out from needle to needle, until it comes entirely loose, then sew; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, put a needle through all the thread double-strong, and tie and pull, and place underneath the thread, and turn your hand from one side and the other, so that some of it comes out; and be careful not to sew, because if you do, it won't be able to be drawn or lifted, and harm will come to the patient; and when you have pulled it all out, put a damp cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on top of the wound's location, and cure until it is sound.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and turned together, and it's not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it askew, but do not cover it; and treat it in the way that we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which we cover the vein is curved, and does not cut it, so that it covers the vein; and it is a thick curve, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but it is coarse as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in hot places where herbs or trees do not grow, and in dry land; and it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body snakes and worms, lodged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this swelling are such that it comes on the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes and the swelling begins to come out, just as a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling bursts open, it's necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth about one and a half palms up to two palms in length, and the node, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time when it comes out at the end, you should wrap around the cloth and the node; and if it is too long, you should cut off part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and don't cut it near its root, until it is entirely come out; because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings an abscess and putrefaction to the place, and a bad disease; for this reason it's necessary that it be treated little by little up to the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this swelling when it is treated grows five palms long, or ten, and one hand has come to me, from which it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, it bursts out a fist or a hole, and it pierces down to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the matter inside should be emptied, and medicine against putrefaction should be applied daily, then it cures like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at any time there are many veins visible, and indeed when it opens in the joint of the foot or the leg, and there is much bleeding from small vessels, and so rain falls; then heal it thus as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "disease of the bull", because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body going up and down, and the person feels it very well as the members go from one to another, until it breaks through the skin where it goes and comes out; and is engendered by corruption of some humors, such as come worms and serpents and lice and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and it reaches the eye, perhaps entering, and destroys the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and drained, one cannot be sure that it is healed: therefore, you must tie the place above and below with a strong tight cord; then strike up and drain it completely; and if the abscess is very deep in the flesh and you do not find it, cauterize with fire on top until it bursts; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming close to the head near the eye, hold a spell under it properly, then strike up and drain it completely; and the patient must use purging of body medicines in order to remove bad humors, and abstain from tainted foods causing corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windfulness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I soon saw it rise as quickly as an ant on the shoulder, like sharp silver when it falls from its place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later it ran through the entire body, until it came into the other arm; then she told me that she had been turning around the body for a while, so I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how she moved from member to member, as I had never seen this disease in that manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had thought many times that pain would often move from one place to another, but I did not see it so in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had cold blood, and her veins were uncovered, and for that reason that constriction appeared; and they did not observe according to this reason those who are full-bodied, and who have moist and well-filled veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see healing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, tie above and below with a bandage hastily, then scrape on top until the swelling is constrained to its place again; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it in your eyes, cure it with those who draw out swellings, such as fetid pills, and viper pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their shapes and according to the places of the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their shape is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and broad-headed ones; and those with two angles, and those with shafts, and those with fragments; and the one that lodges in any member lodges in it either way: or principal member protrudes, such as brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you hereafter appears to you: if it is necessary that you extract this arrow, then beware because death comes after in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes it and penetrates the bone, and the skull fever bursts which is above the brain, is when there are scotoma and deafness and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of gall; and perhaps it appears without a nose or ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost; and there is also a moist white discharge from the wound like pus, and as black as charcoal; and if this sign appears to you, then take care to treat it, and pull out the arrow if it has not entered too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of an arrow wound when it pierces the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it has been stuck in something hard, not hollow; and by chance the arrow moves like hair, and in a black bloody discharge, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: know then without doubt that death ensues.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrowhead which does not penetrate the body is that without foam it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and gasps loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead falls in the covering of the stomach, it is near the small ribs; and makes great anguish and great pain and gasps; and moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead falls on the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat will jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead falls in the belly, and nothing comes out through the intestines first, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead falls in the bladder, and the urine comes out and goes away, and the patient feels very painful, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arm and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and forearm and calf and knee and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you it happened to me, for that reason do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man whose arrow struck him in the eye socket at its root; I tried it and pulled the arrow out from the other side near the ear fat, and he was healed without any trouble.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I tried to pull out an arrow from a boy that struck him in the fat of the eye under the paper under it, and the arrow was bent back, and I could only grab hold of its point towards the bow shaft, and the arrow was big as one from a Turkish bow, entirely made of iron light without ears; the boy was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab at the ear: I drew out the barbs, and delicately pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled out an arrow from the home, which was stuck in his belly, and thought he would die; and then it had passed 30 days, and did not change its disposition; I cut above the arrowhead, and enclosed it, and pulled it out further, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the home was shot with an arrow in his back, and the wound had healed above it; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, to whom an arrow had fallen in his face, and the wound had healed; and thus he remained without suffering great pain; and there were many similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And take out an arrow from the king's person that had been shot into his neck, which was sloping to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was summoned for treatment after it had been stuck in him for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with all a subtle tent, and did not feel it; and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I put on him a poultice attractive and digestive, so that the wound would not swell; and I saw the place of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice every day for many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained so for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I apply a medicinal ointment with corrosive properties to the wound by hand every day, until it is completely open, and I try it, and feel the tip of the arrowhead which is drying out in its place; then I pressed into the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the tip of the arrow appeared visibly; and passed well for 4 months, and then it suppurated so much that I put in tongs, and pulled from one side and the other, and it could not come out; then I did not cease to subtlety and engineer ways with instruments, as long as I caught it in 1 day with good tongs, according to what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, so that I let go and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the nasal cartilage could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may apply your cure to what I do not say; for a book cannot contain everything; but wise masters collect well on small things, and those that are present and defective, find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of limbs or go in through the place where they entered except in two ways: either through the place where they entered them, or from another side; and those that jump out on the other side where they entered are shot into fatty parts, and jump out at least once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump out now, let it stay until the flesh is rotten around it and the issue becomes apparent; and likewise if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it stay for some days and move it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, have it pierced all around with a very sharp instrument, so that the place around it becomes enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the temples of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said occur in the patient: do not pull it out at all, but let it be until it is even after some days, for if the arrow comes to the skull, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck no deeper than in the bone alone, and does not come to the skull, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then the instrument of pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be pulled out, then administer theriacs around it, as I have told you; then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it thoroughly within the tent; and if you feel it, pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then leave the wound until it becomes large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, remove the flesh that is stuck in it from two parts up to the point where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you would pull it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot draw it out at once, then leave it so that the flesh around it becomes rotten, and then draw it out, because the extraction will be revealed.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, then administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter; and beware of cutting into the nerve and the vein, and contrive how to draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid that can be, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from the other side, or if it pierces any part of him, or the skin is swollen where you see or feel it clearly: cut then above it, so that the forceps can take hold of it, and then pull it out: if it jumps back now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it alone and start pulling again until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is in him, then push the whole shaft in; and if the shaft has slipped, and you see administering anointing, administer an instrument sharp, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push it out, and if the arrowhead is stuck, then insert the instrument with the pointed end in to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is lodged, then you must scoop out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it becomes necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has penetrated to the breast or belly or bladder or kidney, and is close, and you can scoop on top, scoop it out; and take care not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to draw out arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, for thrusting into the tip of the arrow, such as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs to put in and to check if there, is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common blood vessels of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins by which one is healed, and there are sixteen that issue from the head, to wit: two pulses that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that appear in the temples; and two veins that are in the hollows of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the crown of the head; and the two jugulars that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips on top of the mouth, and they are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly opened are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head"; and the next one is called "fistula", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and that is the one that is opened, which shows manifestly above the fold.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphena is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the fold of the left side, and the second poplitea is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called "nesse", that is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins underneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting from the veins that are behind the ears, which helps ancient physicians and migraine sufferers; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the patient's head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw until the two veins appear behind the ears in two separate places from the head: then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand above the entire vein, and cut and remove the skin and vein completely in two parts of the arm, and make blood come out as much as you see; then tie and secure it until it is healed.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting from the two arteries that are in the temples, is worth for ancient migraine, and for heat, and for habitual ophthalmia, and for watery eyes; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I say, is: and it is that the patient tightens his neck so that the two veins appear clearly; and feels the pulse under your elbow, and then signals to insert; then lift the skin above the vein in front of your index finger, and insert the lancet below, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done with two other veins, and let blood flow according to your necessity; then release the patient, and put your elbow on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top; and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of its incision and extraction, in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in ancient face diseases, and in migraine, and in gout; and the quality is that the patient twists his neck so tightly that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fossa", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point above the vein, and steady with your hand, or another thing, and let two drops of blood come out according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the bandage for the patient, and tie the vein so it is tied up and there is no bleeding once a large flame has been made.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not advisable that the bleeding be too abundant and cross over, because the bone is close, and perhaps breaks the bleeding when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the armpits helps the eyes, and the itch, and the redness, and the oculist's illness in the eye, and facial diseases; and the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some string, as before; then they bleed, and let the bleeding be about the thickness of a crossbow bolt a little long and a little wide, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bleeding is subtle, it may break through; then let out the blood, as much as you need, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein of the neck is worth against quartan ague and against fevers, and facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes on the face, and most especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient strains his neck, then strains his neck to your left hand, and take the fine flame long, and put it between the two lips in the space that is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the bleeding of the blood according to your necessity, then tie it one night, for it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of the two hives is helpful in constricting the swelling of the vein, and in the beginning of stitching, and in many diseases, and in inflammation, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and eczema; and the quality of the salve is that the patient ties his neck under one and then under the other, as we have said; and the master being on the head of the patient, and the patient sitting under the seat, he then opens the long vein a little wide, then draws out the blood timely, or until it's necessary; then does the opposite in the other vein, then loosens the ligature, and holds the veins moderately so that the patient doesn't choke; and leaves him until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the salve of the books (perhaps a reference to medical texts)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding from the veins above the upper lips helps with mouth ulcers, and gum decay, and cracks in the lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of a vein are to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and know them by that they are black, and by that there are small black spots around them: cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you have doubt, then cut the largest from each side, and do so with the two veins above and below, for it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The veins under the tongue help after the cephalic vein, and that is for the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of a surgeon are that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein: cut one and the other, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat from which one commonly draws blood are treated in two ways: either they prick at a wide flame of myrtle oil, or olive oil that is subtle like surgeons' knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the hot iron lance is very well known, and it is long as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the thick veins with much visible blood and that contain much blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle to pierce, and it is for healing fine wounds, in which there is thin yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him skilfully, and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood starts to flow, then it is necessary to stop it, as I said; and one must not prick the flame, but cut it like "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open up clearly, then you must draw it out, and replace another one with it; or if you wish for some pus to come from it, or if you cleanse the vein in its place within the arm: it opens up clearly; and the swelling in the groin is reduced by heat, just as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you draw out the arm, so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place of the incision, and then bind the arm, and heat the vein with hot iron; and take care that you do not strike in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is an artery: push back then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is arterial blood: hurry then, and put your finger on long, then take out your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it flows fast, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens up, because the head of the vessel [artery] will retract; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fig bark, and make it into a sort of poultice, and take one half and tie well just up to the other half; if the bleeding stops, that's fine; if not, treat with the powder which stops blood; and the stoppage is not at all grievous in more dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vinegar of wine in the middle is so helpful that it treats blood from the head above and the body below, for it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful about the nerve which is below, and if he pierces too deep and finds the nerve, and it swells up and the bleeding is grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then you must stop the bleeding from the instrument with astringent herbs; and push aside the nerve as far as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is blood between the two nerves, cut it of length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.
