The vein of the cephalic is so situated that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and you must bleed with a burning olive oil or with a burning myrtle, for this is the most safe of all veins, since there are no nerves or arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the most gentle place and do not cause harm if you fail the first time, and try again; and perhaps some men's veins become swollen the first time you try, but no harm is done.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the healing is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bleeding is that it is only necessary to preserve health and to prevent illnesses from coming; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are near the navel: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilic; and you should bleed in the morning or early evening, after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and you should bleed on either the first day or the third, two hours or three days after sunrise.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healer who is administering care to the sick does not have a fixed term of office, but rather attends to need at any hour of day or night; and it is not necessary to heal children up until XIV years of age, nor women carrying fruit for just over three-quarters of a month up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one heal the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be healed, in whatever manner that is, it is necessary that they empty their intestines with a light enema, if they have many foul humors retained, so that the veins may not draw out from the intestines the superfluous harmful substances affecting the principal members; nor does one heal who is too full of meat, or drunk, as long as he remains so, or dropsy; and be cautious in healing after a colic fit, vomiting, and bowel evacuation, and multiple cohabitation with women, and travel, watching, and laboring, and all that pertains to virtue, either through cause of the arm or body; then subtilize the humors, if the wound is large, by means of foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then immerse yourself in a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtily cleanse the blood, and heal from the third incision around the waist, as we have said; and keep that day free from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the healer be more elevated than the one being healed, and wipe his hand twice or three times over it, then pull out the thread gently, for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the wound; and then rub it with your hands until the veins fill and can be felt; then moisten the healer's flame with a small amount of old oil; then put the heel of his left hand on top of that incision around the waist where one wants to heal, so that the incision does not burn and fail when hitting.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flow just like strings to the surgeon, and there are such that are filled with air, so that when one puts hot oil on them, they shrink from the heat, and cannot open the vein, and thus one of these; and if the vein bursts open, it is a very narrow wound, for this reason the surgeons should be warned about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the swelling bursts out the first time, it is good; but if not, then it begins again a little below that place or above hastily, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is inflamed and the patient grows frightened, let it be for one or two days and do not bind the arm: perchance there will come abscessed swellings; nor should he enter a bath, then start again with the dressing if it pleases him; and if the wound is small, cut out the core carefully and you doubt that it does not bleed as much as you see, stick to this very same wound with all the hot oil directly; and do the work quickly, just as long as the swelling is inflamed; for this has happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin to stitch it again, and put a little bit of linseed oil on it, because it lightens the body with blood, and is mixed into this place with the oil; and thus administer the linseed oil in each stitch that you make for the veins, so as to stop the flow of blood; and do the same thing with triacle and balm of eyes, when you put it on the place; and separate the flesh from the blood when it gets too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if it comes a large abscess, which occurs many times, especially when it is not stitched tightly until then or the opening of the vein is small, so you hurry and put a moist sponge on the place in water and with oil warm, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding has stopped from the vein, and if there remains some coloration or greenish tint on the place after some days, then it does no harm; and if you see fit, put something made of aloes or myrrh mixed with vinegar, mustard, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess and appearance have occurred in the healing of the Basilica: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the compression of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then be careful not to apply anything from what we have said, for it may cut off the blood from the artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each of the wounds according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see that it is abundant, let it continue until it subsides; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	It is necessary for the one who is weak and worn out, and in need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and to have wider incisions; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and it must be healed gently and often, and one must heal it by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is safe from hemorrhage and severing of nerves, and is better than long or wide cuts.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one to whom the body is weakened by bloodletting, it is necessary to give a wet sponge in the juice of green apples; if he is overheated, then bleed him three or four times with blood; and if he has a cold complexion, then moisten the sponge before bloodletting with a honeyed syrup, or with an aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a sweet-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he spits up blood, after the discharge of fresh blood, then it is necessary that he drinks a broth of meat, and a fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to stretch his arm and heal another time, so it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds in small amounts, little by little, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to stretch his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another part, he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has been heated and brings on fever; thus it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the wound as far as possible before stitching it up; then you must reward all the conditions of spitting up blood, and put your hand on his pulse when he is spitting up blood, so that death may not come in place of the ptoesis, and this happens many times, when the surgeon is negligent; and it does not matter at all when you see him untying the arm, and letting out blood for a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly on it; nor if it is bent, let him extend his arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it alone until he spits up blood again; or you may stick a needle to its point at the flame, as long as the coagulated blood comes out through the wound of the vein, and put on a piece of silk dipped in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let him leave it alone and do not compress it, until the swelling has been reduced.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to bleed again from the blood a second time, you should let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the vein of the head because it is composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the cleaning is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the pus becomes red; then it is tied moderately so that the vein shows well; and then it is cleaned through with a needle not through the length or width, but rather so that the pores are wide; and it is cleaned near the joint of the hand, and if any pus cannot come out, the hand is put in hot water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if this is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the cleaning of this vein is safer from all other veins, than there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cleaning of the vein on the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and it is done like this: extend the hand and put it in hot water until the pus is gone, if one sees it; and if the needle goes awry, and you take out everything at once, nothing hurts; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are under all uncovered of flesh; and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood flow as far as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to close it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do everything similarly to what I told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The patient with the sophene is worthy for all diseases that are under the skin, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its remedy is that the patient dips his foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it is worn out, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins; heal then the most prominent one, or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves which are underneath, and the sap also works in a way as cutting; and the wound becomes useless.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the swelling cannot come out, then put the foot in water again, and let the poultice well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the remedy fails the first time, one must repeat it the second above a poultice, for the place is salty; and do not fear a nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the sophene of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee of strength and its sap is worth for the pain of the loin when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his health is that the patient goes into the bath, and scrapes above the ankle with four threads in twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then he lets blood in all ways that you can, and across; and it's worth noting that you cut him, because the place is clean, and it has been repeated to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't find it, then let blood from him through the vein that is open behind the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and do so much cutting of the blood as you see, and then untie the string, and put on cotton and bind it; now he is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	bloodletting with a cupping vessel
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is made without striking so is in two ways: or it is with much fire, or little fire; and the cupping that is done by striking and extraction of blood is done on 14 places of the body, where one is all over his head; and another is under the neck; and two others are in both sides of the neck; and the cup under the chin; and the cups on the shoulders; and the cups on the buttocks; and the cups on both arms; and the cups on both legs; and the cups on both ankles; and the bleeding does not treat blood, except from small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it has not weakened anyone, just like doing a veinletting; and it is not necessary to administer it, nor with much fire nor little fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if because of necessity of illnesses it is necessary to ventilate, or for habit, let us bring each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and between and in each time; for there are such that, when they have need to ventilate, so they have a heavy head; and those who find repletion and redness on their face, and on their forehead, and neck, and darkening around the eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and bleed; and there are such that sleep, and see through blood and injured and dead and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it's in the middle of the month, we will order to cup after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sowing of the nose so helps to the greyness of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the sowing of the cephalic vein, and it is not necessary for those who are of a cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, for this does great harm to them; and therefore it is not necessary that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold head illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured by it often become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cup a little further down to prevent forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The swelling on the neck is in place of the sinew of the head and the navel; and for this reason it is worthy of the constriction of the intestines, and the tearing of the channel of the womb, and of all the other things; and it needs to be pressed, because if it holds too tightly, it obstructs the intestine or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The swellings on the sides of the neck are worth the pains in the head, and the blindness, and the migraine, and the strangulation, and the pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the sinew of the navel; and you must command the physician that he stretch out his hand to touch, so he does not compress the artery and cause a sudden flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The cuppings under the chin are good for diseases of the mouth and corruption of the gums, and similar ailments that are in the mouth. And it takes the place of the vein-stopping on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The cuppings under the armpits are good for diseases that come from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The swellings of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they suck blood from these large veins; and command the physician that he not cut too deep in front, because the place is bare of flesh, and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cup that is over the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases underneath, and it needs to be large and made of copper, so that it can draw well. And perhaps if it were subtle, it would break through and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cups on the legs are obviously beneficial, because they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains in the hips, thighs, and bladder, and relieve swellings. And they take the place of the two saphenous veins and the two ankle veins. However, they weaken the body after long use and bring paleness to many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the cup is that you first put it on empty, and then seal it quickly, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area red and inflamed, and see the reddish color of the blood; then prick, and remove the cups, and take note of the condition of the body, because there are some who have thick fat, and clear pores: in that case, it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and slightly deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood a little at a time, we can suffice with just one [pricking].
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood to flow, so often should we recommend it; and if the blood is thick, then pierce deeply, and the ends should be that the roots are pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with tough skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the venuises with purifying and dissolving oil: whether it's in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil; and if it's in winter, with cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, you take bitter olive oil, or balsamic oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person whom we heal has soft skin and large pores, then it is not necessary to put oil on them, but rather they should be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of Morel, or cucumber seed water, or porcelain stone water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, should get up with ease, or with hawthorn water, and with sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive swellings are to rise from old wine, or vinegar of themselves, or from a decoction of wormwood or chamomile, or similar things; and they must not be made well with a poultice before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they must not sleep after the fumigation, and it is necessary that he washes himself, when he should be poulticed and when he is poulticed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are sickly with yellow bile, and their blood is too sharp and inflamed; it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and eat small peaches, and mutton fat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, so take honey syrup and aromatic wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and eat small ducks, and eat small peaches and small birds and pigeons; and the day when he will be fumigated, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men some time thyme or musk before fumigation, or after, for the comfort of the main members; and let the blood be diluted, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are applied without hurting are those that are applied to the liver and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the navel and the kidneys and the loins, because those members do not suffer to be hurt upon them, and it is done only in order to attract blood from member to member, such as we put on the shoulders when there is bleeding; to remove the viscosity that is at the member, such as we put poultices on the belly and on the navel to reduce the member; and to remove pain, when there is swelling or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the swelling, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained vapourity, and these poultices are administered empty only to suck; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot medicinal water, such as in the disease of the tearful eye, and in this manner one fills the poultice with warm water only, or with water that has been cooked herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup administered with fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The instrument shall be two palms wide and a half palm deep, and have a small pit on the inside around the middle as if to set in an awl, and it shall be of iron, soft so that it does not hurt the patient when placing it over the limb; and there shall be within it a rod of crossed iron or steel for placing a candle in hold, and the candles shall be large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the poultices of children are different from those of adults, and of thin people than of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must place this poultice over the limb: take the candle of wax or the ointment, and put it inside the poultice in the middle of the rod that is inside the poultice, so that the light is at the bottom of the poultice so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it over the limb, and it should be above the pit that we have said, so that when you want to, the vapor goes out, and remove the poultice; and apply the ointment as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the poultice then which is administered in the illness of pleurisy, has no stick nor tube, and is not applied except when it is full of vinegar, and is placed on the member alone; and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	There are no poultices applied except to members where you cannot put a poultice because of its smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare sores without flesh, such as boils or necrosis, and others like them; and the quality of this poultice is that when you find poultices which are in sweet clear water for piercing, take them; and put one into a sweet clear water, until they become familiar and do not have anything inside; and then bleed with lancet and poultice, then rub the member until it becomes red, and put on the poultices; and when they are full, and swollen, if it is a place where you can put a poultice, put one there, because this helps much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the place of ease first, and then with vinegar, very well, and then press it; and if the place is too wet after the bleeding, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the blood is congealed; and if there are many bleeds, put vitriol paste, or gall, and similar things on it, until it is congealed; or you put hot halves of peeled peas on the place, and leave them until they adhere to the place, and it will now be congealed; and if you need more, take other bleeds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bleeds do not want to take hold, then rub the place of fresh blood on it, or you put a needle in so that the bleed comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are flowing, powder over a bit of alum and burnt silk, or ash, and they will now adhere.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the treatment of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear son, that the foolish men do not know of this chapter, which they have never seen in any ancient book, nor have they read a letter about it; and for this reason is the science estranged in our land, because I never found one good; and I know nothing except by the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments which are provided, as I have done in these two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary therefore that we say the prologue of this book, the sum of speech and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on virtue, so that those who have experienced it know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breaking or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten to cure the patient from this side and that, except if there is weakness of the body, or infancy, or old age; or if the weather is very cold, or too hot; and raw meat, namely cold joints, and fowl and goat flesh, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill themselves too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or spreading of matter to the member; if the patient recovers to their former governance which they used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore itself, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and cheese, and pigs, and beef, and fresh fish, and old wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with good nourishment the bone is repaired more quickly and the break heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well reattached or soldered according to their nature due to the looseness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, like the bones of small children; but have no care, take hold on the broken bone of thick splints which are sturdy and join the member together, as long as it becomes strong again as before; and do not leave any part of your work undone, and for this reason you must feed them on rich meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that broken bones are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is another thing than the break of the rib or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that occur at the angle, and others in splintering, such as the break of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with an open wound, and a break with a small slit throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And it should have its own device and proper instrument in restoration, according to what the memory comes back to its place; and note that the break of the bone is known by that the joint is twisted, and opens well outside, and rings under the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or soning at the toucher, and the patient does not feel great pain, then it has no break; but it can have a twist, or split, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But you must not move it with the hand, but rather put on medications that come later, and then straighten it out slowly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that the breakage which goes in a circle, and are the two parts disjointed, you must now put them in point equal time, so as abscesses chauld I come; and if abscesses chauld I come, so let him remain any day, until the abscess is alleviated; then set it upright at a joint that you can easily and safely, and you should know that the restoration of it is more easy than the restorations of that where there are pieces; then bind, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there is in the bone breakage of pieces, so that it extends to two parts, so if it is hands or feet, or at your hand so it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and at your hand; and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, then reset by all means the additions in their places at a joint that you can, and guard that through your work there does not come to the patient injury or pain; and join well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And be careful with it in your hand if you think it's not well done: straighten it properly, and don't pull or press too hard, as those who do so by their work bring about hot swelling and contraction to the member, as we have warned many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in place, then instruct the patient to stay still so it does not move, neither while watching nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other manner; and make sure that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, then it is not in place, and you must put it into such a condition that it feels no pain; and be sure it is placed correctly, lest it becomes twisted when it is reset; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: then you must envelop them with a soft and subtle linen cloth; and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: then you must envelop them with a wide and strong cord, because the wide cords encircle all the great member, and hold it from all sides evenly, so there is no slackness; then tie around light compresses, three or four according to the member, and grasp your hand on a stick at every cord, then go up above the breakage and hold it less tight, so that the breakage may be slightly distant from itself; and moisten the cord a little by little, until you take a great part of the healthy place, then take another cord, and turn around again above the broken place; then go back to the lower part below the breakage, and hold it moderately, not too hard nor too lightly, as we have said in the first lesson above; then put between the cords compresses made of linen or cloth, until they are entirely even; then tie everything up with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on it, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is an abscess or a swelling, put something soothing and hot on the abscess; and remove the inflammation; and let it be thus for some days; then strain to the stars; and be of half the width of a large reed, cut in a sawing motion, or of wood from which one makes clefts, or of palm tree saplings; and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the star applied to the break is a bit thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it is needed for the member of smallness or largeness; then strain on the stars as you have done at the first wound, then tie above with a thread in the same manner as was done at the first break; the closer, the better; and it must be that the threads are middle-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, like those of the foolish who make their stitches with corded linen yarn, and this is a great error, because the stitch cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it must not have more than two fingers' breadth between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the points of the straps after being tightened in their healthy places, then put underneath them stitches of linen or torn cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the tendon is torn, I will say the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it's not necessary to bind all broken limbs with straps on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the members are large, there is no need to apply a cauterization more than 5 days or 7 after the abscess has occurred, saving; and behold here the manner of old ointments for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and it is that you take wheat flour that holds on to the walls of the mill, and mix with an abundance of egg white, and apply this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of ointment for restoring breakage in many dispositions, and especially among women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring the break, dislocation, and torsion: take 3 parts of asphalt, 1 part of ladanum (a type of resin), 1 part of naphtha, 1 part of gum arabic, 10 parts of musk, 5 parts of myrrh, 14 parts of aloes, 8 parts of alchemil (a type of root), and grind them into powder. Then mix them with abundance of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is good for twisting: take myrrh and spikenard, an equal amount; myrtle and aloes, an equal quantity of nine parts; aloe wood six parts; Armenian balm ten parts, and grind well, and mix with water or an abundance of egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of applying a plaster to joints and bones that have come out of their places, and calming the pain occurring, and the breaking or shattering: take fresh linen, and moisten it with lye and cooked oil, and place it on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not heal, but they are good for calming hot abscesses, and properly remove the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that heals broken bones: take dried leaves of fig and earth leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of applying a plaster to restore the breaking of the bone and to lessen the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of balm, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of wheat, each one in equal parts; and crush them, and mix with vinegar, and if the member is heated, mix with moist coriander water or with water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying plaster more strongly than the first, when a hardened abscess comes to restoring the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wild sage and flaxseed, balm, marigold, and hyssop, and violets and chamomile flowers all in equal part; and grind them up, and mix with salt water or sweet water or wine, according to the warmth of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that for a broken member to be restored well, one should not put anything on it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two [i.e., neither too soft nor too hard].
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to agree that for a broken member to be restored, one should put on it dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is worth for lesion and pain: take musk and hairs from depilated men or feathers from birds, and equal amounts, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave the bandage off for a short time after that, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if not, do not leave it off by hand. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or inflammation, hurry up and remove the bandage now; and take a light cloth, and a moist sponge of the sea, and plunge in water, and lift up the area, so that the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, dampened in water or rose oil, and tie it up with a nut, as long as you are sure of a hot abscess; and calm the inflammation of the member, and remove the pain, then resume the subtle binding, and a little plaster, and do not tighten it so hard as before; and continue until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and inflammation have completely disappeared, and you need to use plaster and bandages again, then repeat it, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not occur in the member of what we have said, do not loosen until after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave twenty days, as one sees, as long as the swelling subsides and approaches the flesh above; then restrain it more than before, and its meat engorges, as I said before; and if you see it drying out more than necessary is, know that inflammation will not come; therefore, soak in warm water thoroughly, every time you loosen it, and apply a poultice for an hour: by this work the inflammation disappears from the member, and quickly heal what the foolish physician did, leaving the member twisted: this is wrong, and is painful work, and I see nothing else but to loathe and do right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Les différentes manières de brisure qui ont été décrites sont :
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways to break and various forms, and the causes are destined; for there are breaks that are made by percussion of a sword, and the shoulder has all the bone cut through just as far as the sicle which is under the bone, so that one who does it is called a "haicheur".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and is called this manner of break "absolute"; and the wounds of these two breaks are great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a crushing blow, or splitting, or from the fist of stone, or falling on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a bursting break, which approaches just to the cloth that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is closed in the bone as subtle as a scratch, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called this break "capillary"; and if the wound that was made or by striking with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of the bone downwards, and the place is hollowed out like when blacksmiths burn above the cauldrons, so that the iron goes in.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to young people whose bones are soft, like the head of an infant; and it happens in all these ways of break that small pieces come off from them as such; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the kinds of breaks by their signs above them, and by the examination that has been done, and by the foul matter that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary sign is known by this: when the bone has been uncovered and one rubs it in with their fingers, if the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the bad symptoms of the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, swelling, paleness, fever, or their pulse to be fast and red, and other similar signs in different conditions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no frightening accident and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first and it's in winter, then it is convenient to take out the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to take out the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone is not corrupted and the accidents that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just up to the cloth that covers the brain, then you must cut into the broken part thus: and it is that you take hold of the patient's head hurt, and uncover above the bone in every way that you can, and on the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if the bleeding of blood comes to reveal the bone, or a boil appears, then you help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the boil is calmed, and be sure of the bleeding of blood; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut on the narrow strip before, and this is the shape
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert another chisel larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a variety of chisels, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of hard iron; and work lightly, so that you don't harm the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, then it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can insert chisels with handles, but not too deeply that they perforate through to the test of the skull, and on top of the point should be a margin or a circle, that doesn't let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one goes in its place of the depth of the bone, so that you have handles for all sides; and this is the shape of the three ways of handles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one handle on top of the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone is pierced; then move the handle to another place a little later, and do all around in this way; then cut with the nippers the space of the bone that is between the piers, and do so more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you bring out the bone into your hand, or onto any of the tools that you have such as tongs, forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and trimmed the bone, then it is necessary that you sharpen the instrument which remains from the bone to all other similar instruments like a chisel, but it must be sharper and more subtle than the other chisel; and if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, then scrape them off with the instruments; then cure the wound with tentatives and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working that Galen says is more sure, and he praises it highly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the break is visible; so that when you have uncovered this part, you will put underneath the head of this incisive lens something of which it is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut from one side, and the part of the body is inflamed in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then tap gently with a small mallet above, so that you lightly scrape the entire bone around it, and take good care to protect the membrane underneath; if it is tightly adhered to the bone, scrape it lightly, because one scrapes well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.
