And if the break in the bone does not penetrate all the way to the thread, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small pieces, then cover up that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp of which you should have various quantities, so as to make it most convenient at each place according to the work and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you pass in front of coarse rasps, and then of finer ones, and do not cease to do this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and subtle breaks, you should make adjustments according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily mastered by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is opened, then it is necessary that you take one linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and put it over the wound; then take another doubled linen cloth in two or three layers, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not hurt the abscess, then administer by placing a bandage on top, and do not tighten it too much until it holds just the wound alone; and leave it thus for one or two days until the abscess is quieted, then untie it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and corn flour, and incense powder, and aristologia, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer further soothing medicines without biting; and be careful that the wound is clean, so you do not leave ointment or let bowels assemble over the dura mater, because when the bowels assemble over the dura mater, they rot and perforate, and cause great harm to the patient; for when one puts something biting on the abscess, it festers above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, for if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no better remedy comes from the medicine that has been put on it, than with such virtue, you must take a part of honey and III parts of rose oil and in glue I drapen, and apply it to the suppurating area; then treat it in manners of cures as it is necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that at no time are the two parts of the nose above or one below alone broken, for they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is crushed or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger or a reed into the eye socket and place the break even with your index finger, in the corner behind, until the eyelid returns to its natural figure; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part of the nose above, and cannot be brought to its place by the finger, it is advisable that you put a small piece of cloth or a bandage on top of the wound, so that it can hold it steady.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, you must do it in this way again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has cooled down, then insert a linen thread into the eye socket, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another cloth on the other part, if it is broken there; and let the folds be so big that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a certain physician that one must moisten the tents with pitch, and move each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is well, but it must be moistened with the mixture of butter, egg yolk, and mill dust; then let the tent remain until the bone is hard and the cartilage stiff.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes bind on or to the nose a pair of goose's quills in place of cloths, and if you have a soft drape around them, and it holds the fracture together, and makes a gentle breeze for the patient to breathe through; then do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put cerot or cotton moistened in rose oil or a little flask of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling of the lump does not come, he should apply an external plaster made from barley flour and incense powder mixed with egg yolk; then put on light fires, and do not cover it with a cloth; and if the break in the bone is small, and it has broken into small pieces, he will take out the splinters with suitable instruments for this, then sew up the fracture, and cure things that ooze flesh and bleeding, with plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the bone, he should treat it with tents, and put in linseed cakes until they are healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	It seems like we've switched to a new topic.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken underneath, and there is no wound outside, and the break is outside alone, and it is not cracked in two, but rather split open inside, then one recognizes this easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is on the right side, that you push your left index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left jawbone, then push your left index finger from the right hand, and gently push the break inside, and secure it with the other hand from outside, and tie equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is split into two, then it is necessary that you administer extension of 1/4 parts [of the jaw] so long as it be equalized.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the dislocation of the teeth has caused movement or wounding, then strain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jaw gum, and place on the gum one double cloth; and place on the cloth a large well-made estelle, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it on with a knot that you can see, and command the patient to rest, and serve light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's face is changing, then take off the splint on the third day, and then put back together what was changed; and apply a poultice on top, with flour mixed with egg or linseed meal powder, after you have removed the gum; and put on a light linen cloth, and if the poultice hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as is until they are healed; many times people heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times [i.e., the poultice and rest].
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, remove no part of the bone that is loosened; be careful to extract it with suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it by flaying according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all of these pieces and none remains, the wound, if it is wide, should be covered with one of the ointments that are prescribed for this purpose to draw out blood, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of great violence
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture is broken multiple times in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two pieces, and has fragments, and this is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such that when the break is without an open wound, you should have two assistants, so that one can hold the splint which feels the fractured part, and the other extend the arm towards the part; then place the break even with your hands, so that the shape be as it should be, and there be no appearance or deformity.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the shoulder of the patient a rounded pole of cloth or linen, and it should be thick according to your necessity; then stretch and lift the splint, and press the pole with your hand, so that you place even the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the end of the splint forward because it goes too deep, it is necessary that the patient lies on their side and places under their shoulder a medium-sized pillow, and have the assistants press the shoulder downward, so that the bone of the splintered part is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the break with your hands, and if you find that it is not properly aligned, it is necessary to split it slightly, and pull out the lighter fragments, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, you should cut at one of the instruments that you have; but place under the splinter this instrument, in order to protect the flesh.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems a spoon, and is not cut off, and be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two handles, such as you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, such as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you split the bones; and when you are sure of hot abscess, if the wound is large, sew up the wound with needle and thread, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms there, it is moistened with a cloth dipped in olive oil, rose oil, and vinegar, and applied.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The splinting of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is that you put on the bone a plaster made of the powder of the mill and of egg yolk, and put on light poultices on top, and place a spear under the axilla, if you need to; then take a very wide band of one palm in width, then put double cloth on top of the poultices, and the plaster; then take a fine splint three inches wide and long, and wrap it around that band so that the end of the band is hanging; and place the splint on the break, and turn the band over the shoulder, and under the healthy axilla, and under the sick axilla; and loosen it from each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the break well, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, so reward it each day, and when the ligature loosens, so restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the axilla, so to lift the shoulder joint high; so it will ease the breaking of the bone by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad events come, until 20 days; then reapply the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and tighten and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most 28 days, and less to some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Il semble que nous avons fini cette transcription d'un texte médical ancien, peut-être du Moyen Âge.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	The shoulder suddenly breaks or loses its proper position and one does not know how it happened; if the appearance agrees with the shape of the break, and resets itself according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then place on the site powdered flour from a mill with an abundance of egg whites, and light bandages, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle splint, a bit larger than the shoulder, and under the splint there are threads in any part of the shoulder, so that you sew those threads with linen strips, so that the splint stays even; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the wound every day; and every time it swells, bind it again, and put the splint back in its proper position, if it has moved out of place, and support the patient on their side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be sure, for it is not bones that get loose quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward and points under the skin, take it out and cauterize it, and do what we have said to alleviate the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet ! La "brisure du pis" se réfère probablement à une blessure ou une fracture du sein (le terme "pis" est ancien et désigne le sein).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this is rare; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, then it falls downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks sense, and dizziness, and by chance may spit blood, and the tendons appear on the broken bone, and he seems to be dead.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back, and they place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and join together the ribs of the two rib bones with their hands, and subtly try to put it in every way you can, so that the shape of the bone be as it should; then place poultices and bandages above the sterile linen of salt or another light wood, and wrap it up in one cloth, and tie it on the broken bone, so that it doesn't move; and turn the cord around to the back, and bind it tightly, and reward each hour with ease, and if it swells, then tighten it; and if it is necessary to untie it, because of corrosion or itchiness that comes to the place, or pain or inflammation, then hasten, and untie it, and scrape off the poultice, and address what has come out in ways of cures; then wash away the poultice, and bind it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	Il semble que nous ayons une section de texte médical du Moyen Âge traitant de la fracture des côtes. Les deux passages que vous avez mentionnés semblent être extraits d'un même texte.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in their large places behind the back, and inside the head, and do not protrude except because they are slippery; and everyone feels it well at the examination of the bones.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the break even, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put a poultice, and tie with an iron band if you need to.

de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken scrotum
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the scrotum are broken many times, and one can see it when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration is that you tie two strings, one above the breakage, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then stretches each member to his part equally; and that is when the breakage is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then it will be one of the ligaments towards the elbow, and the other ligaments beneath the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and then it will be the ligament below the knee, and the extension downward; then place the mirrors on the bone equal with both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the tie, so that abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot swelling, let it cool down then return to your task and treatment; the tie is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap above the fracture with a strong double band in two or three places, and remove the superfluous parts, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the ankle, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, let the end of the thread come up; then turn up the leg and the thigh with the band, then put on the fracture stays, and place a stay on the bone of the leg; then fill in between the leg and the thigh eight linen pads for equal tension, then begin to tie three or four turns above the fracture; and as you go up from the fracture, so loosen the tension; then take the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stays above, then return to the bottom at the end of the thread until it comes below the foot; and if it does not move from its place, leave it so, then if there is no swelling or abscess or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a problem, then untie and adjust what has happened, as we have said many times before. And if there are pieces of bone that protrude, it is necessary to remove them, if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut the area and pull out the splintered bone; and treat it as we have said, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at any time the shin is broken in such a way that stars are put on it, as in the arm and the shoulder; nonetheless, in this restoration made, the patient does not sound.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the shin is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is a small break in the knee joint, but it folds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it's just a small crack or a pit, and has to be treated as all wounds, and with no wound, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put back what was broken to its place, as much as it can be assembled so that you can move it; then put the plaster on, and I put a round splint on it, if you need one, and strain it as it should be, then repair all the preparations that we have said in other breaks, such as applying heat and another appearance; then put on each accident what is fitting for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "femur", not "mustelz", and the other is called "fibula"; and it has all kinds of breakage like the arm when it comes to the bone, and therefore the restoration is done just as with the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns from every side.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, then turn the front side. (i.e. the fibula, which is a thinner and more delicate bone)
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and it can be seen well; and it turns under.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension and put it straight, and tie the splints evenly; but nonetheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly and there are many pieces that the extension be shorter and lighter; and do so according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have completed your work, take two pieces of wooden splint that extend from one part of the leg to the other and are as long as the leg from the knee down. Then wrap them in two loops one on top and the other below, and tie them securely in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and it will be well done. Some people give a single piece of wood as long as the leg, and place it under the leg to prevent movement, and this is properly done in the break where there is a wound; and each day move the leg to see if there is an abscess or other accident. If you treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bone of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes the bones of the foot do break and are shattered, and you must be cautious, for there can be a great deal more damage.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the foot are broken and you see them overlapping each other, then lay such sick person on the ground, as if it were going to walk, and then place his foot upon the other one where the bones are raised, and press down upon them until they return to their proper place; then apply a dressing and bandage over it, and place under the foot of the injured person a small wooden splint with two hooks on it, and bind it securely to the foot properly; then wrap up the foot in a cloth and do other things as you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, untie the splint, for you will find that the bones are aligned, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand. Then place on each broken toe a splint according to its length and somewhat thicker, then put under the foot that wooden splint I mentioned and bind it properly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken toes, place on each one a splint according to their quantity wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind them with the splint under the foot; and let it be so that the end of the splint sticks out from under the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, just as we have discussed them; and treat each case according to what is proper.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone of the wrist.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit and enlarge herself, then incline her to the back part of the body, and hold it from behind; then fill the natural cavity of the patient with cotton, and put in as much as the fist can hold; then throw out the woman, and lift up the back little by little, and thus will the cotton burst forth until it reaches the entrance of nature, and the bone will return to its place with the fist; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or thereabouts: then the breakage will be restored, and if you see that it is not so, take a bladder of thistle, tie a cane to the anus, and insert the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the cane forcefully until the bladder is emptied inside: nature will restore the breakage; then fill with cotton, and let it be thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the shoulder blade of man is broken, or of woman, restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these recent fractures are not hidden from one who puts his study and practice into it and reads this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For breaks signify in many dispositions the right way of restoration: hear then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap cloth around it and let it be for 3 days or so: it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	fracture with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is severe, such as the bones of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be treated now, so that the treatments we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals and it remains with vitriol, if you have nothing else to do, then start again to reset the fracture in the same hour or that day, lest an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess comes there, let the resetting alone until the ninth day, so long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third nor on the fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin's surface, it is necessary that you set it at a light angle with your hands, to slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you don't have the extension handy to set it at an angle with your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the doctor to take three or four of these, as needed in each treatment of a fracture; and let them be round and a large pock, so they don't bend when compressed on the member you're working on, and let them have a groove ahead, and be thick in the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved part should be placed on top of the visible bone; and bind it once, until it returns, and be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the splints cannot well take hold of the bone, then you should enclose the head of the bone, so that the splints have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, take a suitable tool, such as an awl or saw, at your disposal; then scrape out what remains in the bone from sharpness and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is set and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is so that the bone has returned to its place, then soak the cloth in black wine and apply it properly. And do not put cerote or any other oil on the wound, lest it cause corruption; then administer salves when you have restored the bone, and let the wound remain uncovered, and cover all around with a wrapping according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted by the breakage. And many times this has been done by foolish physicians, and death or corruption has occurred over them; and these bandagings are softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that some evil accident will come to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to put salves on it; but wrap around instead of salves, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that pus is forming on the wound, then take off everything you have put on it with vinegar, and apply salve for healing wounds, such as tetrafarmacium ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dress the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is solidified and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be arranged in such a way that the bowstring hangs downwards lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for many days and cannot heal but instead forms a bowstring, know that there are small bones inside, which is why it is necessary to clean the wound with tent (possibly referring to a medical instrument or technique) and remove all these loose pieces of bone that bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess or other kind of corruption comes to the place, then you must cure it, according to what he says in the chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and protrudes on the limb, such as the shin or shoulder bone, and other similar big members, do not pull it out, for many times death ensues, but let it alone until it rots; perchance it will come out after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come on top of the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Bruises come many times after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and perhaps the member cannot do its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the bruise is fresh: if you administer stringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe juice, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with strong vinegar or with egg white or with oil; and apply it to the bruise in compresses, and bind it well, and do not remove it for a day; and then unbind it, and begin another one, as long as the swelling is gone; or you tie on a piece of cloth that has been well made; for the property of cloth is that it removes all the swellings from the members; and if the bruise has already become hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then scrape it off with a scraper, so that its superfluity becomes apparent; or you have it taken out by a barber, as long as it is gone, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is healed, and after the member remains weak and fragile, it happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ties, and the swelling could not come to the member; or due to a multitude of hemorrhages; or due to too great movements, nor in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat well and make their body soft, until the blood is multiplied in them; and give them baths, and give them joy and comfort; then apply poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts to it a great swelling, and brings forth a bloody discharge, as long as the swelling comes to the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is open, and the shape of the member is ugly, although it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one must break the entire limb anew, and many foolish healers have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great evils, and perhaps even death. However, if the swelling and pain are fresh, then they should be drained with hot water or cooked herbs that soothe, such as mulberry leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a soothing plaster, such as a well-made diachylon, and take the juice of mulberry leaves, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on it. Or take ripe figs, and grind them with coltsfoot flaxseed, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is resolved when it is constantly and continuously rubbed with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And gently move the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting has become hardened and stiff, like stone, and needs to be removed with an iron instrument, then it should be carefully cut just up to the bone, with a fine, light incision. And apply a cautery and styptic powder in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of Dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is caused by a joint moving out of its place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to any joint, it should now be reset to its original place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one waits, the swelling will increase, and possibly put pressure on the place; therefore it is not advisable to move it at the hour when it is swollen: many times it brings spasm and other pains; however, when this happens, let the patient be sown, then let him rest until the abscess has been alleviated; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each limb as the treatment comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocation from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Something happens when the jaws are dislocated and they hang down, and the dislocation of both is in two ways: either they are a little pulled out of their place and become a little soft; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and the saliva from the mouth drips that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its proper place by itself in a short while.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it hastily, and not delay; and in such a manner that the ministers show the chief of the patient's mouth, and push the mirror or glass from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is to two parts; and the other do both hands outside, to make equal; and instruct the patient to loosen, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror is placed in its correct position until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is not easy to return, that is, if it are the two jaws together, then warm them up with hot water and oil, until they can be gently rubbed in; do not delay the return, as we said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth is well closed with a soothing salve, he puts on damp cloths in a paste made from rose oil and wax, then ties it lightly with linen threads; and the patient sleeps on his back, and his head should be between two cushions, so that he does not move to right or left, nor tries to speak, but eats light food, until the pains are gone, and the jawbones are closed; and then masticates what he wants lightly, and does not trouble himself to open his mouth to eat and drink, until the jawbone is well closed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be restored to their proper place within an hour and are not returned to their place, it leads to fever and sharp pain, and perhaps colic and maybe vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these things, then know that it is a disaster; and often, in eight days, death comes to the person who has it.
de la forcelle	(dislocation of the jaw)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation of the jaw cannot be released from its original position inside the face and behind the earlobe, and is released only once on the outside, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and stretches out his arms; and then presses the place strongly against your palm, and it will return; then puts on the poultice and bandage, and tightens them; and the head which is near the shoulder cannot dislocate; if not, and if it does dislocate once, he must reset it to its place, as we have said; then puts on the poultice and bandage, and tightens them, and commands the patient to rest until he is healed; and similarly the head of the spine is brought back when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way is when it dislocates to the part of the blade under it; and the second is to the part of the neck; and by chance it dislocates to the top; and it does not dislocate back for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and it dislocates down towards the blade many times, especially in those who have little flesh, because at those it jumps out quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps out slowly, and returns slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that there is a blow or crushing, and the shoulder swells with a hot tumor, and they think it has been dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must then examine it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it falls down towards the blade, and makes a distinction between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them a manifest difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the blade at the toucher the top of the shoulder, just like an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their chest, nor move in any movement; and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you can see it manifestly at the toucher; and this manner of dislocation is not to be reduced when it is new, or if the infant is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the servant lifts the patient's hand up high, then puts his fingers under the arm bone, and lifts the joint with force to its place; and the servant lifts the hand and stretches it out high, then puts it back in. It will come together quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in less than three days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and a soothing ointment should be given him immediately, such as decoction of all-heal and fenugreek and melilot in water, and be administered; then the patient should be placed on his back, and under the shoulder a sheet of linen should be put equal, not too soft nor too hard, then the mire's foot should be placed on the sheet, and with virtuous force the head of the shoulder should be lifted, and the patient's hand pulled; and another minister should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; at once the shoulder comes back into place, and if you see it happening in this manner: then you must have a man who is greater than the patient present, and standing next to him, and push the patient's shoulder under his armpit, and lift up his armpit so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister should pull the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can lift with him some heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And you relieve him in another way: and it is that you drive a long stick into the earth, so that the head of the shoulder is as warm as the handle, and is neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but so that his clothes are softly draped over it, and the patient's hand is extended below on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to come back because of all the things we have said, do this cure: take a stick from two arms long and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded so that it can easily enter into depth under the shoulder blade, in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a cloth on the top of the rod so that the rod does not hurt the patient, and place it under the arm bone of the patient. Then stretch your arm over the long rod and tie the assistant's hand to the rod at the head of the hand, then place the arm on a splint of one wooden board width thick, and let the hands hang down and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that you place under the arm bone a wooden splint of equal thickness, then put the bandage around with miller's powder, incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then stretch it under the arm bone gently, and turn the strap on top of the bandage, and hold the hand against your neck, and let the hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that you check on the patient frequently, until the limbs are comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then check again after five or seven days, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has entered it, or for another reason, then you must apply cauters at three punctures, as it is shown in the chapter on cauters.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things and it comes apart after seven days, and the joint does not hold together, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut, stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs in the chest area, shoulders, or back is caused by a blow or a stretch of the limbs, and another treatment is administered to it; and the treatment continues until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes inflammation and slowness in the movement of the member, then have the patient bathe many times, until that inflammation is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the elbow joint.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and it returns to those points; and it has been dislocated from all sides, as well as in front of and behind, and the dislocation cannot be restored because it can be seen and felt clearly; and dislocation occurs according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient's shoulder with the bone, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to cleanse it immediately, before the pus comes, because if the pus were to come, it would be grievous to remove it; and perhaps cannot be removed entirely, especially when it is in the back; it is worth less than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death will come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is like this when it can be reduced, that you stretch out his hand with your two hands; and his arm should be spread out, and the fingers of the doctor according to the shoulder around, above and below, and push the joint into its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, until it comes back to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand into his other hand, and pushes the shoulder which is dislocated from the root of his palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and have two people extend the arm, and hold it with two hands, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the surgeon has joined the joint to his hand, he rubs it with some oil to lubricate the joint, then presses the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, put on dry plaster with egg yolk, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm at the neck of the patient, and leave him for some days, then unbind.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is strong and in its place, he releases the bandage and lets it be; and if you see that the joint does not heal well, he repeats the plaster and the bandage, and lets it rest for a while, until it is firmly set, then he releases it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, so bathe and scrub him nicely, and press it until it is eased; or put on the joint a woolen poultice, then let it be for a day and a night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint temperately, then put the poultice back on, and then have him enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you see fit, so put on moistened warm cow dung with butter, and apply it above; so it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	Il semble que nous sommes revenus à la question initiale !
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return to its place is light, lighter than other joints Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place immediately, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the place remains swollen, or an abscess forms hotly.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reduction is such that you put the sick hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and the practitioner places them equal, so that he puts his palm above the appearance of the joint, and push it until it returns; however, it is necessary for you to see if it is well in place; then have the patient put the back of her hand on a table at extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, he puts his back of his hand on the table, and the physician puts his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, it is well If not, he strains with soothing plasters the swelling boils, and lets them be in this way without continuing again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back into place after some days, the twisted joint remains; and no harm comes to the patient until the hand is moistened, and he can strain nothing at all: then know that the nerves are severed, or the arteries; for there is no other cause worse than straining by fire near the case, and perhaps it does not amount to anything else.
