Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have said, then strain and leave it for 5 days, then release and let it be like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well and there is any swelling, then soak the hand in hot water and rub it until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Dislocation of the wrist (or forearm). It seems like we've been reading a medieval medical text on how to treat this condition!
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the tendon of the hand is dislocated to each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or belly; then they are bent, and push the dislocation into the pouches until it returns, then support the head of the tendon, and pull it towards the place where it was disjointed; and let it be for two days, and then make it even on that day; and from then bind it, as we have said, and unbind it from day to day, and move it, and tie it again; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same thing if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do just as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	The dislocation of the spine (vertebrae) of the back. Another potentially serious medical condition!
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or if there are more than one that are dislocated, there is no cure, for the bone quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations jump out without will, and cannot hold them, and many times soften some member, either the two hips or both arms or one And many times move the scapula to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you return if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure nor recovery whatever.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of cures by great words say it has no great benefit in all; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have made instruments in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbosity that comes to the chest before, there is no cure nor health; and similarly that which comes straightly on both sides, and one cannot cure further than that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient lie stretched out on his face in an equal place, and have a bandage underneath him so he does not bleed; then stick two skewers into the head in the earth strongly, and another at the feet, and tie a string behind the joints of the patient, and another behind the thighs, and knees, and ankles; and two servants know the strings, one to the head and the other to the feet, among the two skewers; and be well closed, the skewers as we have said, and the attendant put his palms on the spine strongly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not come back by this cure, then take a table of three arms' length, and sharpen the edge underneath, and the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the table underneath the vertebra, then put the middle part of the table on the spine; and have the doctor's feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until it comes back to its place; and if you see fit, do the same in the vertebra that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two wooden splints of one arm's length and a little more, with two others going towards the feet; and have between each splint, on top and underneath, a space of one palm in length; and have in each splint one groove where the tendon runs, and let the splints be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of splints have another smaller splint of one palm's length to turn the tendon; then tie the string which is among the tendons near the head, and the other string near the feet to the other tendon; and each of the attendants turn their own tendon up to all the strings, and the master straighten out the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is evened out, apply desiccating ointment with abundance of egg, and then bandage, and then attach an iron plate three digits long, which will strengthen the place of the armpit and the part of the spine that was injured; then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use a gentle poultice on the patient until they are healed; and if any thing comes to pass at the end of their healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines with the iron plate which we have spoken of before; and one time I administered a piece of pork fat, and one time an appearance came in the lower part of the spine next to the back, and they thought it was dislocation; but this is the bone that is cracked, for which reason you must not have any presumption: by chance it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	The Dislocations of the Hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder are prone to dislocations alone, and it is not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is displaced in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inwardly towards the contrary side, and somewhat displaced in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of his dislocation is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased kneecap is more prominent than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend their knee at the fire; and the place which is near the inflamed abscess is hot.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one whose dislocation is in the back is that this accident is contrary to those in the front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one whose dislocation is in the front are that they bend their leg well according to its completion; however, they do not double their knee with pain, and if one wants them to walk, they cannot move forward, and retain their urine, and swell the ankle, and when they go, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one whose dislocation is in the back are that they cannot straighten their knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the tendons of the thigh are at the place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this condition of dislocation are that you return to see if the dislocation is ancient, and it remains in its position, then there is no cure; and one must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of three manners of dislocation, then hurry to turn the joint inward and outward, and move it from right to left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, you must have strong ministering and bind the leg strongly with two hands, or with one string that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand thus so that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then he tightens with a single thread above the crotch; and another pinches the chief of the string; and all stretch up and down at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and hangs.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to all three appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, so it is necessary to apply treatment to its resemblance. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot compress it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two legs of the patient together with a strong soft lien on both heels and on both knees, and the ill leg be stretched out two thumbs more than the others; then let it be hung from the head of a beam, and suspended over the ground by long arms; then command the servant to grasp the backside of the hip, and have another servant hang with the patient, who grasps firmly the backside, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at its farthest point, let the patient lie down as we have said in the case of gilbertia, and stretch the lien properly on the ill leg and on the thigh; then put two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then stick a torch between the hips of the patient inside the form; and there be placed moistened cloths around so that he does not injure himself, then each servant extend towards him, and the physician place his hand in equal balance on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put them on the table, and press them thus as we have said in the procedure for a boil, and place the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the sick leg hastily and as I have said; and the physician should place their hand over the painful ankle, then press with the other hand and stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it should not stretch the patient downwards, nor lift them up from the earth, but rather they should be placed as if the hip had been dislocated in front, as we have said about lying on two hips; and place a bandage over their face, and extend the strap as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be correct when the patient stretches out their legs and they are even; then put the splint together and tie with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and have them rest for three days or four, then release the splint and place the emplastrum on it; and if you see that they are even, then strain it, as before, and let them rest for three days; then release the splint and make them walk gently until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	The Dislocation of the Knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee joint is displaced in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and backward; and it does not get displaced forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg up to their knee, and if it does not straighten at their knee, know that they are dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and put your back on their face, and place their foot on your feet; then take their kneecap in your palms, and pull it between your elbows, then bend the two sides of the kneecap together; and another servant stretches their foot, so that the kneecap returns to its place, and the sign is that they have straightened their leg a little lightly; and put the poultice on top, and make the leg rest at the knee, and hold them together tightly for three days or four, then loosen them; and the patient should not work until the members are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer a strong stretching force, as we have said in the treatment of the scrotum, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	The Dislocation of the Ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle is sometimes sprained and sometimes completely dislocated, both inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and stretch before the part where it is dislocated: the return to place is light, and one must stretch it lightly with their hands when it is just moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit up straight, and the servants stretch out a cloth by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with your left two times, then stretch it upwards, and push the foot firmly upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, repeat the work, because it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and place a sturdy board firmly in the earth between their thighs, and tie cloths around, so that the patient does not hurt themselves; then have one of the servants stretch out the foot with their hands or with a cord, so they can bind it above the heel; then each servant should stretch equally, and the board be thus between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when one stretches them; then place the physician's hand equal on either side of the dislocation in their hands, and another of the servants will press down on the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is put in place, then one applies the poultice and stops above, and ties with a cloth, and binds the foot to the leg, and guards the nerves which are above the heel at the back, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leaves him two or three days, and if the bandage loosens, reties it; then unbinds on the third day or the fourth, and keeps the patient from going for four days; and if he goes before the appointed time, it's not certain that it will not dislodge again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, then you must alleviate them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	The Wrist
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the wrist is dislocated, it should be stretched carefully without great effort, and it's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any new swelling of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit on a level surface or on a table straight out, and place your foot over what protrudes from these joints, then press firmly with your foot until it returns; and when it is even, and there is nothing protruding, put under the sole of the foot a board two feet long, then tie firmly, and leave him three days, then unbind; and have him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Wounds and Dislocations Together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at first soothing remedies on hot abscesses, and let the patient be in God's hands if you do not see hope of salvation; and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the hot abscess may come; and when the member is at its place, administer soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and treat the wound, as it seems proper, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a break, and small bones are disjointed, then take them out, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this will be your undoing according to your Creator, and because of the knowledge that will arm you and protect your body.
Amen	So be it
